Defending Prophet David from False Stories
Author refutes false stories about David and Uriah, citing Ali's condemnation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author defends Prophet David against false narratives and explains that prophets' repentance reflects their profound reverence for Allah.

Core Idea
False stories about prophets violate their sanctity and must be rejected.

The author directly confronts distorted accounts about Prophet David that have circulated in Israelite traditions. He not only rejects these stories but also provides a powerful quote from Ali ibn Abi Talib condemning those who spread them. Finally, he explains that David's repentance and supplication are entirely consistent with the prophets' deep awe and veneration of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the author's firm tone and the flow from rejecting false stories to explaining prophetic behavior.
The passage contains a quote from Ali and a theological explanation.
2
Identify the false story being rejected
The author alludes to a story about David and Uriah that implies David desired the killing of a Muslim. Identify how he refutes this idea.
He says 'it should not be thought of a prophet that he loved the killing of a Muslim.'
3
Examine Ali ibn Abi Talib's condemnation
Read Ali's statement about flogging those who narrate the false storytellers' version. Understand the severity of violating the sanctity of a prophet.
Ali said he would flog them twice.
4
Understand the explanation of prophetic repentance
The author clarifies that David's weeping and supplication are normal for prophets because of their intense veneration, fear, and awe of Allah based on their knowledge.
This reframes the story positively.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
داود وأوريا خبرٌ يثبتُ ، ولا يُظَنُّ بنبي محبةُ قتل مسلم وقيل : إِنَّ الخصمينِ اللَّذين اختصما إليه في نِتاجِ غنم ، ظاهر الآية ( انتهى (١) على قلتُ : ولا شكٍّ أنَّ في كتب بني إسرائيل في هذه القصَّةِ تخليطاً عظيماً لا يليقُ أَنْ يُلتفتَ إليهِ ، وقد قالَ علي بن أبي طالب رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ : ( مَنْ حَدَّثَ بما قال هؤلاءِ القُصَّاص في أمرٍ داود .. جلدتُهُ حدَّينِ ؛ لِمَا ارتكبَ مِنْ حرمةِ مَنْ رفعَ اللهُ قدرَهُ ((۲) وأما استغفارُه عليه الصلاة والسلام وبكاؤُهُ وتضرُّعُهُ : فجار على المعهودِ مِنْ حالِ الأنبياء عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام في إجلالهم المولى الكريم ، وخوفهم منه ، وهيبتهم له على قَدْرِ معرفتهم به .
David and Uriah is a story that is established, and it should not be thought of a prophet that he loved the killing of a Muslim. And it was said: The two opponents who came to him [David] with a dispute about the breeding of sheep (is the meaning of the verse?). I say: And there is no doubt that in the books of the Children of Israel regarding this story there is great confusion that is not worthy of attention. And Ali ibn Abi Talib, may Allah be pleased with him, said: 'Whoever narrates what these storytellers say about the matter of David, I will flog him twice; because of what he has violated of the sanctity of one whose rank Allah has raised.' And as for his [David's] asking forgiveness, peace be upon him, and his weeping and supplication, that is in accordance with the customary state of the prophets, peace be upon them, in their veneration of the Generous Lord, their fear of Him, and their awe of Him according to the extent of their knowledge of Him.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage defends Prophet David (peace be upon him) against false narratives. The author first states that the story of David and Uriah is established but should not be misinterpreted to imply that David desired the killing of a Muslim. He then mentions an alternative interpretation that the dispute was about sheep. The author asserts that the Israelite accounts are corrupted and should be ignored. He quotes Ali ibn Abi Talib, who threatened to flog anyone who repeats the false storytellers' version, as it violates the prophetic dignity. Finally, the author explains that David's repentance, weeping, and supplication are consistent with the prophets' behavior: they intensely venerate, fear, and stand in awe of Allah according to their profound knowledge. The passage thus clarifies the correct understanding of the incident and rejects distortions.

Key Terms
داود
أوريا
قصاص
حرمة
أنبياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume David intended to kill Uriah to marry his wife.
Correction: The author shows this is a false narrative from corrupted Israelite sources and that it is unthinkable for a prophet to love killing a Muslim.

Checkpoint
What did 'Ali ibn Abi Talib threaten to do to those who narrated the false story about David?
A) Execute them
B) Flog them twice
C) Imprison them
D) Excommunicate them

Key Takeaway
The sanctity of prophets must be upheld; false stories about them are to be rejected, and their actions like repentance are expressions of their deep reverence for Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have heard stories about prophets that might not be in the Quran or authentic sunnah. When you hear such stories, do you immediately reject them or do you entertain them? The author says the Israelite books have 'great confusion' and are not worthy of attention. Are you willing to flog your own curiosity and stop seeking captivating stories about prophets, even if they seem harmless? Will you commit to only learning about prophets from the Quran and authentic hadith, no matter how boring the true account might seem?
?
Ali ibn Abi Talib said he would flog anyone who narrates false stories about David. Think about the stories you've heard in lectures or on social media about prophets—do you ever share them without verifying? If you do, you are violating prophetic sanctity. From this day forward, will you fear Allah enough to stop spreading any tale about a prophet unless you know it is authentic? Will you take a stand against falsehood even if it means contradicting popular speakers?
?
David's repentance was not because of sin, but because of his immense veneration and fear of Allah. When you repent, is it because you are truly in awe of Allah's majesty, or is it just a routine? The prophets' awe is proportional to their knowledge—you cannot fake it. Will you strive to increase your knowledge of Allah so that your repentance becomes a genuine act of veneration, not just a habit?

The Prophet's Marriage to Zaynab: Divine Command and Legislation
Author explains the true account of the Prophet's marriage to Zaynab, guided by divine revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the true account of the Prophet Muhammad's marriage to Zaynab as a divine command and legislative ruling, and the reasons for the Prophet's initial concealment of revelation.

Core Idea
The Prophet's marriage to Zaynab was purely by Allah's command, not personal desire.

This passage addresses a controversial story that critics have used against the Prophet. The author clarifies that only the Qur'anic account is correct, and explains the divine wisdom behind the events. We will see how the Prophet acted in perfect obedience, concealing revelation until the proper time and then openly declaring it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the full translation. Let the author's narrative flow through the story.
Notice the Qur'anic verse that forms the core of the argument.
2
Identify the legal ruling established
The passage states that Allah married Zaynab to the Prophet to legislate the permissibility of marrying the wives of adopted sons. Find this in the text and understand its significance.
This ruling is a central point of the story.
3
Trace the Prophet's actions and reasons
Follow the sequence: the revelation before Zayd's divorce, the Prophet's advice to Zayd, his concealment of revelation, and final acceptance. Ask yourself: why did the Prophet act this way?
The commentary will help clarify the divine wisdom behind each step.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأَمَّا قصَّةُ نبينا وسيّدِنا ومولانا محمَّدٍ صَلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ مَعَ زيدٍ مولاه وزينب رضي الله تعالى عنهما : فليسَ يصح فيها إلا ما ذكر مولانا جلَّ وعزّ في كتابه العزيز ؛ مِنْ كونه سبحانه وتعالى زَوَّجَ لنبينا عليهِ الصلاة والسلام زينب بعدَ فِراقِ زيد لها ، وشرع بذلك إباحة تزويج حلائل الأدعياء ، وأَنَّهُنَّ لا يُلحَقْنَ في التحريم بحلائل أبناء النسبِ فقال جلَّ مِنْ قائل : ﴿ فَلَمَّا قَضَى زَيْدٌ مِنْهَا وَطَرًا زَوَحْنَكَهَا لِكَيْ لَا يَكُونَ عَلَى الْمُؤْمِنِينَ حَرَجٌ فِي أَزْوَج أَدْعِيَا بِهِمْ إِذَا فَضَوْا مِنْهُنَّ وَطَرًا ﴾ [الأحزاب : ٣٧] . وقد أوحى الله سبحانَهُ إلى نبيِّنا عليه الصلاةُ والسلام بما أرادَ مِنْ تزويج زينب لهُ قبلَ أَنْ يُطلقها زيدٌ ، فلمَّا أُلْقِيَ فِي قَلْبِ زِيدٍ حُبُّ فراقها ، ومُنِعَ مِنَ المتعة بها لمَّا قَرُبَ أوانُ حرمةِ أُمومتها لجميعِ المؤمنين ، وهيبة قربها مِنْ سيّدِ ولدِ آدمَ ، وأشرف خلْقِ اللهِ أجمعين . . جاءَ يشكو تعاظمها عليهِ للنبيِّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، وأَنَّهُ يريدُ فِراقَها ، فأمرَهُ عليهِ الصلاة والسلام بإمساكها ، وتقوى الله في شأنها ؛ عملاً بالظاهرِ الذي أُمِرَ أنْ يحكم به ، وأخفى عليه الصلاةُ والسلام عن زيد وعن غيرِهِ ما في نفسِهِ الطاهرة المطهَّرَةِ مِنْ وَحْيِ اللهِ تعالى له بأنَّ زيداً يفارقها ، وهي زوجة له بعده ؛ حياءً منهُ عليهِ الصلاة والسلامُ أنْ يُظهِرَ ذلكَ وزينب بعد في عصمةِ زيدٍ ، ولأنَّ ذلكَ أيضاً مِنَ العلم الذي لم يُؤمَرُ بإظهاره للناس في ذلك الوقتِ . فلما فارقها زيد رضي الله تعالى عنه ، وزَوَّجَها المولى تبارك وتعالى منه عليه الصلاةُ والسلام .. قَبِلَ وانقاد ، ودخل عليها بلا إذنٍ ولا مؤامرة ؛ مبالغةً منهُ عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلام في إظهار الرضا بعطيَّةِ المولى جل وعلا ، وأنساه حينئذ التعظيم لجنابِ المولى تبارك وتعالى والحياء منه الالتفات إلى مقالة الناس ، والحياءَ مِنْ زيدٍ أو غيرِهِ ، واتَّصف في ذلكَ بما وصف الله تعالى به إخوانَهُ مِنَ الرُّسُلِ في قولِهِ جلَّ وعزّ : ( الَّذِينَ يُبْلَغُونَ رِسَلَتِ اللَّهِ وَيَخْشَونَهُ وَلَا يَخشَونَ أَحَدًا إِلَّا اللَّهُ وَكَفَى بِاللَّهِ حسيبا الأحزاب : ۳۹] ، وحينئذٍ باحَ عليه الصلاةُ والسلام بما أوحى الله تعالى إليه في شأن زيد وزينب ، ولم يخش أحداً مِنَ الخَلْقِ
As for the story of our Prophet, our Master, and our Liege, Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, with Zayd his freed slave and Zaynab, may Allah be pleased with them both: nothing is correct in it except what our Liege, Glorious and Mighty, mentioned in His Noble Book; that He, Exalted and High, married our Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, to Zaynab after Zayd had separated from her, and by that He legislated the permissibility of marrying the wives of adopted sons, and that they are not included in the prohibition like the wives of biological sons. So He said, Glory be to the Speaker: {So when Zayd had accomplished his desire from her, We married her to you so that there should be no difficulty for the believers concerning the wives of their adopted sons when they have accomplished their desire from them} [Al-Ahzab: 37]. And Allah, Exalted, had revealed to our Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, what He willed of marrying Zaynab to him before Zayd had divorced her. So when love of separation from her was cast into Zayd's heart, and he was prevented from taking pleasure with her because the time had drawn near for her to become forbidden as a mother for all believers, and due to the awe of her closeness to the Master of the children of Adam and the most honorable of all creation, he came complaining to the Prophet, peace be upon him, of her being too great for him, and that he wanted to separate from her. So the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, ordered him to keep her and fear Allah in her matter, acting according to the outward command he was ordered to judge by, and he, peace and blessings be upon him, concealed from Zayd and others what was in his pure, purified soul of the revelation of Allah, Exalted, that Zayd would leave her and she would be his wife after him; out of modesty, peace and blessings be upon him, to reveal that while Zaynab was still under Zayd's protection, and also because that was knowledge he was not commanded to disclose to people at that time. So when Zayd, may Allah be pleased with him, left her, and the Lord, Blessed and Exalted, married her to him, peace and blessings be upon him, he accepted and submitted, and entered upon her without permission or consultation; as an exaggeration from him, peace and blessings be upon him, in showing satisfaction with the gift of the Liege, Glorious and High, and at that time [Allah] made him forget, out of veneration for the Majesty of the Liege, Blessed and Exalted, and modesty before Him, any heed to people's talk, and modesty before Zayd or anyone else. And in that he was characterized by what Allah, Exalted, described his brothers among the messengers in His saying, Glorious and High: {Those who convey the messages of Allah and fear Him and do not fear anyone except Allah, and sufficient is Allah as a Reckoner} [Al-Ahzab: 39]. And at that point he, peace and blessings be upon him, divulged what Allah, Exalted, had revealed to him concerning the matter of Zayd and Zaynab, and did not fear any of creation.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage defends the prophetic integrity in the story of Muhammad's marriage to Zaynab. The author begins by stating that only what Allah mentions in the Qur'an is correct: Allah married Zaynab to the Prophet after Zayd divorced her, to establish the ruling that adopted sons' ex-wives are not forbidden like biological sons'. The author then explains the sequence: Allah had already revealed to the Prophet that Zaynab would be his wife before Zayd divorced her. Allah placed love of separation in Zayd's heart and prevented him from enjoying her because the time approached for her to become a 'mother of the believers' (i.e., the Prophet's wife). Zayd came complaining to the Prophet, who advised him to keep her and fear Allah, acting on the apparent ruling. The Prophet concealed the divine revelation about the future divorce out of modesty, as Zaynab was still Zayd's wife and he was not commanded to disclose it. When Zayd divorced her and Allah commanded the Prophet to marry her, he accepted without consulting anyone, to show complete satisfaction with Allah's gift. Allah made him forget any concern for people's opinions, and he acted like the other messengers who convey Allah's messages and fear none but Him. Finally, he openly declared the revelation about Zayd and Zaynab, fearing no one. The passage thus explains the divine wisdom and the Prophet's perfect obedience.

Key Terms
زيد
زينب
أدعياء
حلائل
الحياء
الوحي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some critics claim that the Prophet acted out of personal desire in marrying Zaynab.
Correction: The passage shows that the marriage was purely by divine command and for legislation. The Prophet concealed the revelation until the proper time and accepted the marriage as an act of obedience, not desire.

Checkpoint
Why did the Prophet initially advise Zayd to keep Zaynab and fear Allah?
A) He wanted to marry her himself
B) He was following the outward command, since revelation had not yet come to disclose the future
C) He wanted to test Zayd's obedience
D) He was afraid of people's criticism

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's marriage to Zaynab was a divinely commanded act that established a legal precedent, and the Prophet's concealment of revelation was out of modesty and obedience to Allah's timing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you willing to obey Allah's commands even when they conflict with what people expect of you, or when they might make you appear inconsistent in the eyes of others? The Prophet followed the outward command while hiding inner knowledge—do you have the courage to obey outwardly even when you know the full story might be misunderstood?
?
When you know something that could cause criticism if revealed, do you trust Allah's timing and remain silent like the Prophet did, or do you feel compelled to defend yourself immediately? Is your modesty before Allah greater than your fear of being misunderstood?
?
The Prophet accepted the marriage without consultation, showing complete satisfaction with Allah's gift. Is there any gift from Allah in your life—whether a trial or a blessing—that you are resisting because you worry about what others will say? What would it take for you to accept it wholeheartedly, fearing only Allah?

The Verse of Praise: Defending the Prophet's Modesty
Sanusi refutes the misinterpretation of the verse as blame.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the verse 'And you fear the people' is actually praise for the Prophet's beautiful character, not a rebuke.

Core Idea
The verse praised the Prophet's modesty, not blamed his fear.

Sanusi defends the Prophet (peace be upon him) against a common misinterpretation of Quran 33:37. Critics have claimed the verse rebukes the Prophet for fearing people, but Sanusi shows it is a commendation of his noble character. Let's examine the passage to see how he argues this.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the strong opening refutation.
The author uses the phrase 'لَا خَلَاقَ لَهُ وَلَا أَدَبَ' to dismiss critics.
2
Identify the core claim
The author asserts the verse is 'مدح' (praise), not 'عتب' (blame). Underline these two key terms.
3
Understand the explanation
The 'fear' is explained as modesty. Allah commanded to prioritize His fear over people's. This shows the Prophet's beautiful character.
The phrase 'الخلق الجميل والطبع الكامل' summarizes the praise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: {وَتَخْشَى النَّاسَ وَاللَّهُ أَحَقُّ أَن تَخْشَاهُ} [الأحزاب: 37] فَلَيْسَ فِيهِ عَتْبٌ عَلَيْهِ كَمَا يَعْتَقِدُهُ مَنْ لَا خَلَاقَ لَهُ وَلَا أَدَبَ وَلَا فَهْمَ وَلَا دِينَ، وَإِنَّمَا هُوَ مَدْحٌ لَهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ بِالْخُلُقِ الْجَمِيلِ وَالطَّبْعِ الْكَامِلِ؛ وَهُوَ الْخَشْيَةُ مِنَ النَّاسِ؛ أَيِ الْحَيَاءُ مِنْهُمْ يُقَابِلُهُمْ بِمَا يَسُوءُهُمْ، ثُمَّ أَمَرَهُ سُبْحَانَهُ أَنْ يُرَبِّحَ خَشْيَتَهُ وَالْحَيَاءَ مِنْهُ عِنْدَ وُرُودِ أَمْرِهِ عَلَى الْحَيَاءِ مِنَ النَّاسِ، وَهَكَذَا كَانَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ فِي هَذِهِ الْقَضِيَّةِ وَغَيْرِهَا، لَا يُبَالِي بِشَيْءٍ إِذَا حَضَرَهُ حَقُّ اللَّهِ تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى.
As for His statement, the Exalted: {And you fear the people while Allah is more deserving that you fear Him} [Al-Ahzab: 37], there is no blame in it upon him as those who have no good, nor etiquette, nor understanding, nor religion believe. Rather, it is praise for him, peace and blessings be upon him, for his beautiful character and perfect nature; and it is the fear of the people, i.e., the modesty from them, he faces them with what displeases them. Then He, glorified, commanded him to make his fear and modesty of Him overcome his modesty of the people when His command came, and thus was he, peace and blessings be upon him, in this matter and others, not caring for anything when the truth of Allah, blessed and exalted, was present.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage defends Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) against the misinterpretation of the verse 'And you fear the people while Allah is more deserving that you fear Him' (Quran 33:37). The author states that this verse is not blame (عتب) as some ignorant people claim, but rather praise (مدح) for the Prophet's beautiful character (الخلق الجميل) and perfect nature (الطبع الكامل). The 'fear of people' (الخشية من الناس) is explained as modesty (الحياء) from them, such that he would treat them with what displeases them out of politeness. Then Allah commanded him to prioritize fear and modesty of Him over modesty of people, and the Prophet obeyed. The passage emphasizes that the Prophet did not care for anything when the truth of Allah was present.

Key Terms
الخشية
الحياء
العتب
المدح
الخلق الجميل
الطبع الكامل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'And you fear the people' is a rebuke of the Prophet.
Correction: The verse is actually praise for his beautiful character and modesty, as the author explains.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the verse 'And you fear the people' actually indicate about the Prophet?
A) It is a blame for his fear of people.
B) It is praise for his beautiful character and modesty.
C) It shows he was commanded to fear people more.
D) It indicates he was afraid of people's reactions.

Key Takeaway
The verse is praise for the Prophet's modesty, and Allah commanded him to prioritize fear of Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a specific moment this past week when you held back from saying or doing something right because you were afraid of how others would react. How does the Prophet's example of prioritising Allah's command over people's opinions challenge you to act differently next time? What will you do to prepare for that situation?
?
The Prophet faced people with what displeases them out of modesty—yet he did not let their feelings stop him from obeying Allah. Is there a truth you are avoiding speaking because it might upset someone close to you? Are you willing to sacrifice that comfort for Allah's sake? Write down one step you can take this week to speak up.
?
Allah commanded the Prophet to make His fear overcome modesty from people. In your own life, which 'people' are you most afraid of displeasing—your family, friends, colleagues, or community? How can you actively train yourself to place Allah's pleasure above theirs, starting today?

Defending Prophet Yusuf's Brothers: No Prophethood at the Time of Action
Author defends Yusuf's brothers by stating they were not yet prophets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reasoning behind defending Yusuf's brothers by establishing that they were not prophets at the time of their actions.

Core Idea
Yusuf's brothers were not prophets when they acted, so no contradiction.

This lesson addresses a common objection regarding the story of Prophet Yusuf. Critics might question how the brothers, later considered prophets, could have treated Yusuf so harshly. The author, citing Qadi Iyad, clarifies that their prophethood had not yet been established at that time, removing any apparent contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the author's argument.
Notice the quote from Qadi Iyad.
2
Identify Qadi Iyad's two arguments
Qadi Iyad gives two reasons: (1) the brothers' prophethood was not established, (2) they were young. Find these in the text.
The second argument is supported by the verse about playing.
3
Understand the significance of the commentators' clarification
The commentators explain that the mention of 'tribes' in the Qur'an refers only to those who were given prophethood, not all the brothers at that time.
This reinforces Qadi Iyad's point.

وَأَمَّا قِصَّةُ يُوسُفَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَإِخْوَتهِ: فَلَيْسَ فِيهَا عَلَى يُوسُفَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ عَتْبٌ. وَأَمَّا إِخْوَتهُ: فَقَالَ الْقَاضِي عِيَاضٌ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: (لَمْ تَثْبُتْ نُبُوَّتُهُمْ فَيَلْزَمَ الْكَلَامُ عَلَى أَفْعَالِهِمْ، وَذِكْرُ الْأَسْبَاطِ وَعَدُّهُمْ فِي الْقُرْآنِ عِنْدَ ذِكْرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ .. قَالَ الْمُفَسِّرُونَ: يُرِيدُ: مَنْ نُبِّئَ مِنْ أَبْنَاءِ الْأَسْبَاطِ، وَقَدْ قِيلَ: إِنَّهُمْ حِينَ فَعَلُوا بِيُوسُفَ مَا فَعَلُوا كَانُوا صِغَارًا، وَلِهَذَا لَمْ يُمَيِّزُوا يُوسُفَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ حِينَ رَأَوْهُ، وَلِهَذَا قَالُوا: {أَرْسِلْهُ مَعَنَا غَدًا يَرْتَعْ وَيَلْعَبْ} [يوسف: 12]، وَإِنْ ثَبَتَتْ لَهُمْ نُبُوَّةً فَبَعْدَ هَذَا) (١)
As for the story of Yusuf, peace be upon him, and his brothers: there is no blame upon Yusuf, peace be upon him, in it. As for his brothers: Qadi Iyad, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'Their prophethood has not been established so that one would have to discuss their actions. And the mention of the tribes (al-asbat) and their counting in the Qur'an alongside the mention of the prophets – the commentators said: He means those who were given prophethood from among the sons of the tribes. And it has been said that when they did what they did to Yusuf, they were young, and for this reason they did not recognize Yusuf, peace be upon him, when they saw him, and for this reason they said: {Send him with us tomorrow to enjoy and play} [Yusuf: 12]. And if their prophethood is established, it was after this.'
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage addresses potential objections to the story of Prophet Yusuf (peace be upon him) and his brothers. First, it states that there is no blame (عتب) on Yusuf in the story. Then it defends the brothers by quoting Qadi Iyad, who argues that their prophethood was not established at the time of their actions, so there is no need to discuss their deeds. The mention of the tribes (الأسباط) in the Qur'an alongside prophets is interpreted by commentators to mean only those among the sons of the tribes who were actually given prophethood. Furthermore, it is suggested that the brothers were young when they acted, which explains their failure to recognize Yusuf and their request to 'play.' If they later became prophets, it was after this incident.

Defending Prophet Yusuf: The Grammar of Innocence
Author explains the grammatical construction to show Yusuf did not intend sin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the grammatical analysis of Quran 12:24, particularly the use of 'lawla' and the concept of taqdim wa ta'khir, affirms Prophet Yusuf's sinlessness and protects his prophetic dignity.

Core Idea
Yusuf's desire was grammatical, not actual — the Quran defends his purity through precise linguistic structure.

This passage defends Prophet Yusuf (peace be upon him) against the apparent implication of the verse 'and he would have desired her if it were not that he saw the proof of his Lord' (Quran 12:24). By closely examining the Arabic grammar, the author shows that the intended meaning is a hypothetical scenario that never occurred. The use of 'lawla' and the rhetorical device of forward-backward ordering (taqdim wa ta'khir) are key to understanding that Yusuf was protected from any actual sinful intent.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get a sense of the overall argument. Notice that it begins by addressing the verse and then gives the preferred grammatical interpretation.
Pay attention to the terms 'waqf', 'istinaf', and 'taqdim wa ta'khir'.
2
Identify the key grammatical elements
Identify the placement of the stop (waqf) after 'hammat bihi', the resumption (istinaf) of the next phrase, and the forward-backward ordering. Understand how these change the meaning.
The phrase 'lawla' is crucial: it indicates that the conclusion (desire) is prevented because the condition (seeing the proof) occurred.
3
Connect to the theological point
Reflect on how the grammatical analysis protects Yusuf from any accusation of sin. The verse quoted at the end ('Thus, that We might turn away from him evil and lewdness') reinforces his protection.
The footnote mentions different grammatical schools; it's an additional nuance but not essential for the main point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: {وَلَقَدْ هَمَّتْ بِهِ وَهَمَّ بِهَا لَوْلَا أَن رَّأَى بُرْهَانَ رَبِّهِ} [يوسف: 24]: فَالْأَقْرَبُ أَنَّ الْوَقْفَ عَلَى قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: {وَلَقَدْ هَمَّتْ بِهِ}، وَيُسْتَأْنَفُ قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: {وَهَمَّ بِهَا لَوْلَا أَن رَّأَى بُرْهَانَ رَبِّهِ} عَلَى التَّقْدِيمِ وَالتَّأْخِيرِ (٢)؛ أَيْ: لَوْلَا أَنْ رَأَى بُرْهَانَ رَبِّهِ لَهَمَّ بِهَا، وَقَدْ عُلِمَ أَنَّ (لَوْلَا) تَقْتَضِي امْتِنَاعَ جَزَائِهَا لِوُجُودِ شَرْطِهَا، فَيَكُونُ هَمُّ يُوسُفَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ بِهَا مُنْتَفِيًا لِرُؤْيَتِهِ بُرْهَانَ رَبِّهِ. وَيَدُلُّ عَلَى حِفْظِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مِنْ كُلِّ سُوءٍ هَمًّا كَانَ أَوْ غَيْرَهُ .. قَوْلُهُ جَلَّ وَعَلَا: {كَذَلِكَ لِنَصْرِفَ عَنْهُ السُّوءَ وَالْفَحْشَاءَ إِنَّهُ مِنْ عِبَادِنَا الْمُخْلَصِينَ} [يوسف: 24]. (في هامش ( و ): ( قوله: «تقديم» وهذا بناء على مذهب الفراء المجوز لتقديم الجواب، أما على مذهب سيبويه ومن تبعه فالجواب محذوف، والمتقدم على الشرط دليله، قرره م س ).
As for His statement, the Exalted: {And she certainly desired him, and he would have desired her if it were not that he saw the proof of his Lord} [Yusuf: 24]: The closest is that the stopping is upon His statement, the Exalted: {And she certainly desired him}, and His statement, the Exalted: {and he would have desired her if it were not that he saw the proof of his Lord} is resumed with forward and backward (في التقديم والتأخير); meaning: if it were not that he saw the proof of his Lord, he would have desired her. And it is known that (lawla) necessitates the prevention of its conclusion due to the existence of its condition. So Yusuf's desire for her is negated because of his seeing the proof of his Lord. And there indicates his protection, peace be upon him, from every evil, intent or otherwise, His saying, mighty and majestic: {Thus, that We might turn away from him evil and lewdness. Indeed, he was of Our chosen servants} [Yusuf: 24]. (In the margin of (و): (His saying: 'forward' – this is based on the school of al-Farra' who permits placing the answer forward. As for the school of Sibawayh and his followers, the answer is omitted, and what comes before the condition is evidence of it, as determined by M.S.).
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage defends Prophet Yusuf (peace be upon him) against the apparent implication of the verse 'and he would have desired her if it were not that he saw the proof of his Lord' (Quran 12:24). The author provides a linguistic analysis to show that Yusuf did not actually intend sin. The preferred interpretation is that the stopping (الوقف) in recitation is after 'And she certainly desired him,' and then the phrase 'and he would have desired her if it were not that he saw the proof of his Lord' is a new sentence with forward and backward (تقديم وتأخير), meaning the condition is placed after the result for rhetorical effect. Thus the meaning is: 'If it were not that he saw the proof of his Lord, he would have desired her.' The particle 'lawla' (if it were not) indicates that the conclusion (the desire) is prevented because the condition (seeing the proof) occurred. So Yusuf's desire is negated. The author then cites another verse (12:24) that states Allah turned away from him evil and lewdness because he was among the chosen servants. The footnote adds a grammatical point: al-Farra' allows placing the answer (the conclusion) before the condition, while Sibawayh says the answer is omitted and the part before the condition is evidence of it.

Key Takeaway

The Status of Yusuf's Brothers: Prophethood Not Established
Qadi Iyad argues that the prophethood of Yusuf's brothers is not established.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Qadi Iyad argues that the prophethood of Yusuf's brothers is not established and how this protects prophetic integrity.

Core Idea
The actions of Yusuf's brothers do not undermine prophethood because their prophethood is not established.

This passage examines a common question: were the brothers of Prophet Yusuf prophets at the time of their actions? Qadi Iyad provides a nuanced answer that safeguards the integrity of prophets while acknowledging the ambiguity in the Qur'anic text. We will explore his argument and the evidence he cites.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to understand Qadi Iyad's claim.
Notice the quote structure and the supporting evidence.
2
Identify the two arguments
Find the two main points Qadi Iyad makes: the interpretation of 'al-asbat' and the possibility that the brothers were young.
These are the key reasons why their prophethood is not established.
3
Understand the conditional conclusion
Note the final statement: 'if their prophethood is established, it is after this.' This preserves the possibility while clarifying the event.
This shows the careful approach of scholars in matters of prophetic history.
4
Reflect on the theological significance
Ask yourself why this matters: it protects the reputation of prophets and explains how the Qur'an mentions 'al-asbat' without contradiction.
Keep in mind the broader principle that actions of non-prophets do not affect prophetic infallibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا إخوتُهُ : فقالَ القاضي عياض رحمهُ الله تعالى : ( لم تثبت نبوَّتُهم فيلزم الكلام على أفعالهم ، وذِكْرُ الأسباط وعدهم في القرآنِ عند ذكر الأنبياء .. قال المفسرون : يريدُ : مَنْ نُّبيَّ مِنْ أَبْناءِ الأسباط ، وقد قيلَ: إنَّهم حينَ فعلوا بيوسف ما فعلوا كانوا صغاراً ، ولهذا لم يميّزوا يوسف عليه السلام حين رأوه ، ولهذا قالوا : أَرْسِلْهُ مَعَنَا غَدًا يَرْتَعْ وَيَلْعَبْ ﴾ [يوسف : ۱۲] ، وإن ثبَتَتْ لهم نبوَّةً فبعد هذا )
And as for his brothers: al-Qadi Iyad (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'Their prophethood has not been established, so discussion of their actions is not obligatory. And the mention of the tribes (al-asbat) and their enumeration in the Qur'an alongside the mention of the prophets... the commentators said: He means: those among the sons of the tribes who were prophets. And it has been said: When they did what they did to Yusuf, they were young, and for this reason they did not recognize Yusuf (peace be upon him) when they saw him, and for this reason they said: "Send him with us tomorrow to enjoy himself and play" [Yusuf 12:12]. And if their prophethood is established, it is after this.'
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage presents the view of Qadi Iyad regarding the status of Yusuf's brothers. The author cites him to clarify that the brothers' prophethood is not certain, so their actions (like selling Yusuf) cannot be used to criticize prophets. He notes that the Qur'an's mention of 'al-asbat' refers to those among them who were prophets, not all of them. Some scholars say the brothers were young at the time, hence their actions are excused. Even if they were prophets, it was after this event.

The Grammatical Defense of Yusuf
Sanusi explains the grammatical structure and uses 'lawla' to defend Yusuf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the grammatical reading of the verse and the function of 'lawla' negate any sinful desire from Yusuf.

Core Idea
Yusuf's desire was negated by the proof he saw; grammar proves it.

Sanusi begins by tackling the controversial verse directly, showing that a correct grammatical pause and the particle 'lawla' entirely remove any implication of sin from Yusuf. This lesson walks through that linguistic argument and its supporting verses.

Guided Path
1
Understand the pause issue
Learn why the pause after 'hamat bihi' matters and how 'taqdeem wa ta'kheer' changes the meaning.
The author says the closest view is to pause after 'wa laqad hammat bihi'.
2
Analyze 'lawla'
Realize that 'lawla' negates its result when its condition exists, so Yusuf's desire is negated because he saw the proof.
'Lawla' requires negation of the apodosis.
3
See the supporting verses
Note how other verses (24, 32, 23) confirm Yusuf's protection from evil.
These verses are quoted as evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَلَقَدْ هَمَّتْ بِهِ وَهَمَّ بِهَا لَوْلَا أَن رَّمَا بُرْهَانَ رَبِّهِ ﴾ [يوسف : ٢٤] : فالأقربُ أنَّ الوقفَ على قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَلَقَدْ هَمَّتْ يه ) ، ويُستأنف قوله تعالى : وَهَمَّ بِهَا لَوْلَا أَن رَّمَا بُرْهَانَ رَبِّهِ ) على التقديم والتأخير (۲) ؛ أي : لولا أن رأى برهانَ رَبِّهِ لهم بها ، وقد عُلِمَ أنَّ ( لولا ) تقتضي امتناع جزائها لوجودِ شرطها ، فيكون هم يوسف عليه السلام بها منتفياً لرؤيتِهِ برهان ربَّهِ . ويدل على حفظِهِ عليهِ السلامُ مِنْ كل سوء هما كان أو غيره .. قوله جل وعلا: كَذَلِكَ لِنَصْرِفَ عَنْهُ السُّوءَ وَالْفَحْشَاء إِنَّهُ مِنْ عِبَادِنَا الْمُخْلَصِينَ ﴾ [يوسف : ٢٤] ، وقال تبارك وتعالى : ﴿ وَلَقَدْ رَوَدتُّهُ عَن نَفْسِهِ، فَاسْتَعْصَمَ ﴾ [يوسف : ۳۲] ، وقال جلَّ مِنْ قائل : ﴿ وَغَلَقَتِ الْأَبْوَبَ وَقَالَتْ هَيْتَ لَكَ قَالَ مَعَاذَ اللَّهِ إِنَّهُ رَبِّي أَحْسَنَ مَنْوَاكَ إِنَّهُ لَا يُفْلِحُ الظَّلِمُونَ ) (يوسف : ٢٣) قيل في ) ربِّي ) : إنَّهُ اللهُ ، وقد قيل : إن معنى ( هم بها ) أي : بزجرها ووعظها ، وقيل : بضربها ودفعها ، وقيل : هم بها : غمها امتناعه عنها • ويحتمل أن يكون المراد : همَّ بسببها ؛ أي : أصابَهُ هم بسببِ هذه المحنة التي وقعَتْ فيها مِنْ معصية المولى تبارك وتعالى وما كابدَتْهُ مِنَ المشاق والشَّعَفِ بحبّهِ عليهِ الصلاة والسلام ، فودَّ عليه السلام على سبيل الرحمة لها ألا تكونَ وقعَتْ في شَيْءٍ مِنْ ذلكَ مِنْ أجله ، لكنَّهُ عليهِ السلامُ لمَّا رأى ببصيرته برهانَ أُلوهية المولى العظيم وعدله تبارك وتعالى في جميع أفعاله وأحكامه .. سلَّمَ ورضي ، وزال همه بها ، فيكون المعنى على هذا : لولا أن رأى برهانَ رَبِّهِ لدامَ هَمُّهُ بها ، أو يكون المعنى : لولا أن رأى برهانَ رَبِّهِ لسعى فيما يُخلِّصُهَا مِنْ هذه المحنة ، ويُسكِّنُ عليها بعض لوعةِ الاشتياق إليه ولو بوعد منه لها في المساعدة على ما أحبَّتْ منهُ ، أو نحو ذلكَ ممَّا يُترخَّصُ بِهِ في الظاهر على سبيل التورية ؛ لضرورة الدفع عن نفسه وعنها ، لكن منعه من الالتفات إلى شيءٍ مِنْ ذلك رؤيتُهُ عليهِ السلام برهانَ رَبِّهِ الدال على كمال مُلكيَّتِهِ للعبيدِ ، وأنَّهُ المنفرد بالتدبير والحكم ، ونفوذ المشيئة والاقتدار ، لا معارض لهُ في حُكمِهِ ومُلْكِهِ ، فلا يليق بالعبدِ الفقير المضطر العاجز الجاهل إلا السمع والطاعة ، والانقياد لنهيه
And as for the saying of the Most High: 'And indeed she did desire him, and he would have desired her if it were not that he saw the proof of his Lord' [Yusuf 12:24]: the closest (interpretation) is that the pause is on His saying: 'And indeed she did desire him', and His saying: 'and he would have desired her if it were not that he saw the proof of his Lord' is resumed with fronting and delaying; that is: had he not seen the proof of his Lord, he would have desired her. And it is known that 'lawla' necessitates the negation of its result due to the existence of its condition. Thus Yusuf's desire (hamm) for her is negated by his seeing the proof of his Lord. And that which indicates his protection (peace be upon him) from every evil, whether desire or otherwise, is His saying, Glorified and Most High: 'Thus, that We might turn away from him evil and immorality. Indeed, he was of Our chosen servants' [Yusuf 12:24]. And He, Blessed and Most High, said: 'And indeed, I have sought to seduce him, but he remained chaste' [Yusuf 12:32]. And He, Glorified and Exalted said: 'And she locked the doors and said: Come to me! He said: I seek refuge in Allah. Indeed, he is my lord, who has made good my residence. Indeed, wrongdoers do not prosper' [Yusuf 12:23]. It is said regarding 'my lord' (rabbi) that it means Allah. And it has been said: The meaning of 'he desired her' (hamm biha) is by rebuking her and admonishing her. And it is said: by hitting her and repelling her. And it is said: 'he desired her' means he grieved for her because of his abstention from her. And it is possible that the intended meaning is: he was concerned because of her; i.e., he was afflicted with concern because of this trial that she fell into due to disobedience to the Master (Blessed and Most High) and what she endured of hardships and infatuation with his love (peace and blessings be upon him). So he (peace be upon him) wished, out of mercy for her, that she had not fallen into any of that because of him. But when he (peace be upon him) saw with his insight the proof of the divinity of the Great Master and His justice (Blessed and Most High) in all His actions and judgments, he submitted and was pleased, and his concern for her ceased. Thus the meaning according to this is: had he not seen the proof of his Lord, his concern for her would have continued. Or the meaning is: had he not seen the proof of his Lord, he would have striven to deliver her from this trial and to calm for her some of the pain of longing for him, even by a promise from him to help her in what she desired from him, or something like that which is permissible outwardly by way of dissimulation (tawriya) due to the necessity of repelling harm from himself and from her. But his seeing the proof of his Lord (peace be upon him) prevented him from turning to any of that, because it indicates the perfection of His ownership of all servants, and that He alone is the disposer and judge, and the executor of will and power, with no opponent to His judgment and dominion. Thus nothing befits the weak, needy, compelled, ignorant servant except hearing and obeying and submitting to His prohibition.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is an exegetical discussion defending Prophet Yusuf (peace be upon him) from any sinful intention. The author begins by explaining the correct grammatical interpretation of the verse. He argues that the pause (waqf) should be after 'And indeed she did desire him,' and then the phrase 'and he would have desired her if it were not that he saw the proof of his Lord' is read with fronting and delaying (taqdeem wa ta'kheer), meaning that Yusuf's desire was conditional upon not seeing the proof. Since he did see it, his desire was negated. He then supports this with other verses that affirm Yusuf's protection from evil. Next, he presents several interpretations of 'he desired her' (hamm biha) that remove any suspicion of sin: some say it means he intended to rebuke or admonish her, others say he intended to hit or repel her, and others say it means he was grieved for her due to her infatuation. He then elaborates on the interpretation that Yusuf was concerned for her well-being, wishing she had not fallen into trial because of him, but upon seeing the proof of God's sovereignty, he submitted and his concern ceased. The author concludes that Yusuf's seeing the proof prevented him from any course of action that might violate divine command. Throughout, the author emphasizes that prophets are protected from sin.

Key Terms
هم
لولا
تقديم وتأخير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Yusuf had a momentary sinful thought before being stopped.
Correction: The verse's grammar shows his desire never occurred because the condition for it (not seeing the proof) was absent.

Checkpoint
What is the effect of the pause and taqdeem wa ta'kheer on the meaning of the verse?
A) It makes the desire actual and then negated.
B) It makes the desire conditional on not seeing the proof, so it never happened.
C) It shows Yusuf desired but was stopped.
D) It has no effect on meaning.

Key Takeaway
The grammatical structure and the particle 'lawla' prove that Yusuf's desire was entirely negated by his seeing the proof of his Lord.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever convinced yourself that a fleeting sinful thought is harmless, unlike an actual sin? How does Yusuf's complete negation of even the desire confront that reasoning? Will you commit to purifying your heart from the very first inclination?
?
When you face temptation, what 'proof of your Lord' have you seen—perhaps a verse, a reminder of accountability, or a glimpse of Allah's mercy—that you have ignored? What will you do this week to actively seek and heed those proofs before desire takes root?
?
Yusuf was protected because he was of Allah's chosen servants. But you are not a prophet—does that mean you are excused from striving for similar purity? What steps will you take today to become one of those whom Allah shields from evil, even in your thoughts?

Sinless Interpretations of 'Hamm'
Sanusi offers sinless lexical and theological interpretations of Yusuf's hamm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand multiple sinless interpretations of Yusuf's 'hamm' and the theological reason for his submission.

Core Idea
Every reading of Yusuf's 'hamm' absolves him of sin.

After establishing the grammatical defense, Sanusi presents various lexical and contextual interpretations that exonerate Yusuf. Each meaning removes any hint of sin, culminating in a profound theological reflection on his seeing the proof of his Lord.

Guided Path
1
Explore the lexical alternatives
Learn the different interpretations of 'hamm biha': rebuking, hitting, grieving, or being concerned.
Each interpretation is sinless.
2
Understand the concern interpretation
Yusuf was concerned for her affliction, but his concern ceased upon seeing the proof of God's sovereignty.
This shows his mercy and submission.
3
Grasp the theological conclusion
Seeing the proof prevents any action contrary to divine command, emphasizing total submission.
The proof includes God's ownership and sole authority.

عليهِ الصلاة والسلام ، فودَّ عليه السلام على سبيل الرحمة لها ألا تكونَ وقعَتْ في شَيْءٍ مِنْ ذلكَ مِنْ أجله ، لكنَّهُ عليهِ السلامُ لمَّا رأى ببصيرته برهانَ أُلوهية المولى العظيم وعدله تبارك وتعالى في جميع أفعاله وأحكامه .. سلَّمَ ورضي ، وزال همه بها ، فيكون المعنى على هذا : لولا أن رأى برهانَ رَبِّهِ لدامَ هَمُّهُ بها ، أو يكون المعنى : لولا أن رأى برهانَ رَبِّهِ لسعى فيما يُخلِّصُهَا مِنْ هذه ?

?
The moment Yusuf saw the proof of his Lord, his worldly concerns vanished and he submitted completely. Is there an area in your life where you are still resisting God's decree—trying to manage outcomes yourself instead of surrendering? What would it cost you to lay that burden down today?

Yusuf's Innocence by Divine Protection Only
Sanusi asserts that Yusuf's innocence was solely by divine protection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Prophet Yusuf's escape from sin was entirely due to Allah's success and protection, not his own strength.

Core Idea
Yusuf's purity was a gift from Allah, not his own achievement.

Sanusi affirms a core Sunni belief about prophets: their sinlessness is a divine gift. In this passage, he applies this specifically to Prophet Yusuf's famous trial with the wife of al-Aziz. By quoting the Quran, Sanusi shows that it was Allah's intervention that kept Yusuf pure.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and English translation. Notice the structure: a claim followed by a Quranic proof.
Pay attention to the term 'الصديق' (as-Siddiq), an epithet of Prophet Yusuf.
2
Identify the claim
Sanusi asserts that everything good that happened to Yusuf, specifically his avoidance of sin, occurred only by Allah's tawfiq (success) and isma (protection).
The word 'إنما' emphasizes exclusivity – nothing else caused it.
3
Understand the proof
Sanusi supports his claim with Quran 12:24, where Allah states that He turned away evil and lewdness from Yusuf because he was among His chosen (mukhlaseen) servants.
This verse directly attributes Yusuf's innocence to Allah's action, not Yusuf's own will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكلُّ هذا إنَّما حصل للصديق عليه الصلاة والسلام بتوفيق المولى تبارك وتعالى وعصمتِهِ ، كما قالَ جلَّ مِنْ قائل : ﴿ كَذَلِكَ لِنَصْرِفَ عَنْهُ السُّوءَ وَالْفَحْشَاء إِنَّهُ مِنْ عِبَادِنَا الْمُخْلَصِينَ ﴾ [يوسف : ٢٤]
And all of this occurred for as-Siddiq (Yusuf), peace be upon him, only by the success of the Lord, Blessed and Exalted, and His protection, as the Mighty among speakers said: {Thus did We turn away from him evil and lewdness; indeed, he was of Our chosen servants} [Yusuf: 24].
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is a statement that everything good that happened to Prophet Yusuf (the Siddiq) — particularly his avoidance of the sin proposed by the wife of Al-Aziz — was entirely due to divine success (tawfiq) and protection (isma) from Allah, not from his own strength or will. The author cites the Quranic verse (Yusuf 24) as proof, where Allah explicitly states that He turned away evil and lewdness from Yusuf because he was among Allah's chosen, protected servants. This affirms that prophets are protected from sin by Allah's grace.

Key Terms
الصديق
بتوفيق المولى
عصمته
المخلصين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophet Yusuf avoided sin by his own strong will and moral character.
Correction: The passage and verse clarify that his avoidance was solely due to Allah's success and protection (tawfiq and isma), not his own power.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what enabled Prophet Yusuf to avoid sin?
A) His own strength of will
B) Divine success and protection
C) The warnings of his father
D) Fear of social punishment

Key Takeaway
Prophet Yusuf's innocence was a direct result of Allah's protection, confirming the doctrine of prophetic isma (sinlessness).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you successfully avoid a sin, do you instinctively credit your own willpower, or do you recognize Allah's tawfiq? How does this lesson rewire your understanding of your own 'goodness'?
?
Yusuf was protected because Allah chose him as one of 'al-mukhlisīn'. Do you live with the urgency of being among that group, or do you assume you are safe without actively seeking Allah's protection?
?
The particle 'إنما' restricts the cause of Yusuf's purity to Allah alone. Where in your life are you subtly claiming credit for your own moral successes, and how can you consciously redirect that praise to Allah today?

Defense of Prophet Musa's Actions
Sanusi defends three actions of Prophet Musa from charges of sin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi defends Prophet Musa's actions by showing the killing was unintentional, his words were acts of prophetic adab, and his fear was out of awe, not sin.

Core Idea
Prophet Musa's 'sins' are actually acts of righteousness and prophetic humility.

The stories of the prophets in the Quran sometimes raise questions about their actions. Here, Sanusi addresses three potential objections against Prophet Musa. He explains that the killing of the Egyptian was accidental, his attribution of the act to Satan was a mark of good manners, and his plea for forgiveness was a habitual expression of awe, not a confession of sin. This passage clarifies the prophetic character and the high station of prophets before Allah.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
Before diving into the passage, recall that prophets are sinless. This lesson addresses apparent objections to that doctrine. The author, Sanusi, is defending Prophet Musa.
2
Read the Arabic passage
Read the full Arabic passage aloud or silently. Notice the three distinct segments: the killing, the statement about Satan, and the statement about wronging oneself.
The footnote from Imam ar-Razi is supplementary.
3
Examine the first defense
Identify how Sanusi argues the killing was unintentional. Look for the key terms: 'وكز' (struck) and 'غير عمد' (not intentional). Understand that Musa intended to help the oppressed, not to kill.
4
Examine the second defense
Analyze why Musa's words 'This is from the work of Satan' are interpreted as good adab. Note that the devil's assumption was mistaken because Musa is protected from sin.
This shows prophets can attribute actions to Satan without sinning.
5
Examine the third defense
Understand that Musa's apology 'I have wronged myself' is a custom of fear and reverence, not an admission of sin. Prophets know they are not held accountable, yet they express humility.
The footnote from ar-Razi reinforces this idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما خبرُ موسى عليه الصلاة والسلام مع قتيله الذي وكزَهُ : فقد نص الله تعالى أنَّ القتيلَ مِنْ عدوِّهِ ، وإنَّما قصد عليه السلام إغاثة الملهوفِ الإسرائيلي ، فوكز العدو القاهرَ لهُ بنيَّةِ دفعِهِ عَمَّنِ استولى عليه ، فصادف موتَهُ مِنْ غيرِ عمدٍ. وقولُهُ عليهِ السلامُ : هَذَا مِنْ عَمَلِ الشَّيْطَانِ ﴾ [القصص : ١٥] حَسْنُ أدب. منه في نسبة الفعل المحبوبِ للشيطانِ إليه ، ولم يحبُّه الشيطان هنا لإيقاعِهِ الكليمَ في معصية ؛ لأنَّهُ معصوم منها ، بل لتوهم الشيطان ذلك توهماً أخطأ فيه وخابَ فِيهِ ظَنُّهُ. وقوله عليه السلام : ﴿ ظَلَمْتُ نَفْسِي فَاغْفِرْ لي ﴾ [القصص : ١٦] جري على المألوف مِنْ خَوْفِ الرُّسُل والأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلامُ مِنَ اللهِ تعالى خوف هيبة وتعظيم وإن علموا عدم المؤاخذة مِنَ المولى تبارك وتعالى ، ولهذا اعتذروا في الموقفِ بما علموا عدم المؤاخذة به ، وعلى هذا يُحمَلُ استغفارُ الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام وخوفهم (۱). (۱) وهذا ممَّا عبّر عنه الإمام الرازي في مفاتيح الغيب » ( ٧ / ١١٤ ) بقوله : ( جميع الطاعات في مقابلة حقوق إلهيته جنايات ، وكلُّ أنواع المعارف الحاصلة عند الخلق في مقابلة أنوار كبريائه تقصير وقصور وجهل ، ولذلك قال : ﴿ وَمَا قَدَرُوا اللَّهَ حَقَّ قَدْرِهِ ﴾ [الأنعام : ۹۱] ، وإذا كان كذلك فالعبد في أي مقام كان من مقام العبودية وإن كان عالماً جدّاً . . إذا قوبل ذلك بجلال كبرياء الله تعالى صار عين التقصير الذي يجب منه الاستغفار )
As for the story of Musa, peace be upon him, with his slain whom he struck: Allah the Exalted stated that the slain was from his enemy, and he (Musa) only intended to aid the oppressed Israelite, so he struck the overpowering enemy with the intention of repelling him from the one he had seized, and his death occurred accidentally without intent. And his statement, peace be upon him: 'This is from the work of Satan' [Qasas: 15] is good manner from him in attributing the beloved action to the devil. And the devil did not desire this to cause the interlocutor (Kaleem) to fall into sin, because he is protected from it, but rather due to the devil's false assumption, in which he was mistaken and his opinion failed. And his statement, peace be upon him: 'I have wronged myself, so forgive me' [Qasas: 16] is conducted upon the accustomed manner of the messengers and prophets, peace be upon them, of fear of Allah the Exalted—a fear of awe and veneration—even though they know there is no reproach from the Lord, Blessed and Exalted. For this reason, they apologize in the station with what they know there is no reprisal for, and upon this is carried the seeking of forgiveness of the prophets, peace be upon them, and their fear (1). (1) This is among what Imam ar-Razi expressed in 'Mafatih al-Ghayb' (7/114) saying: 'All acts of obedience in comparison to the rights of His Divinity are crimes, and all types of knowledge attained by creation in comparison to the lights of His Majesty are deficiency, shortcoming, and ignorance. Therefore He said: {And they did not appraise Allah with true appraisal} [al-An'am: 91]. And if this is so, then the servant, in whatever station he may be among the stations of servitude, even if he is extremely knowledgeable... when compared to the majesty of the glory of Allah the Exalted, becomes the very deficiency from which seeking forgiveness is obligatory.'
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is a defense of Prophet Musa against accusations of sin. It deals with three issues: (1) the killing of the Egyptian, (2) his statement 'this is from the work of Satan', and (3) his statement 'I have wronged myself'. The author first argues that the killing was unintentional and for a righteous purpose (helping the oppressed). Second, Musa's attribution of the action to Satan is reinterpreted as good adab, not as a claim that he sinned; the devil's hope that Musa would sin was mistaken because Musa is protected. Third, his saying 'I have wronged myself' is explained as a habitual expression of fear and awe of Allah, not a confession of actual sin, since prophets know they are not held accountable for minor slips. The footnote from Imam ar-Razi reinforces that even the best acts of worship are negligible compared to Allah's majesty, so seeking forgiveness is always appropriate for servants out of humility, not necessarily sin.

Key Terms
وكز
إغاثة الملهوف
غير عمد
حسن أدب
خوف هيبة وتعظيم
مؤاخذة
استغفار الأنبياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Prophet Musa committed sins: he killed a man, blamed Satan, and confessed wrongdoing.
Correction: The passage clarifies: the killing was unintentional; attributing to Satan was good manners; and the confession was out of awe, not sin.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why did Prophet Musa say 'I have wronged myself'?
A) He acknowledged a real sin
B) It was an expression of fear and awe of Allah's majesty
C) He was confused about his actions
D) He wanted to deceive the people

Key Takeaway
Prophet Musa's actions, when understood in context, are consistent with prophetic infallibility—they demonstrate righteous intention, good adab, and profound humility before Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make a mistake, do you immediately assume the worst of yourself, or do you consider your intent as Musa's intent was considered? How can you train yourself to judge your own actions by intention rather than outcome?
?
The prophets seek forgiveness for things they are not held accountable for—do you have that same overwhelming awareness of Allah's majesty that makes you apologize for even your good deeds? If not, what is holding you back?
?
If someone wrongs you with an accidental harm, how often do you assume bad faith instead of granting the benefit of the doubt? How does this lesson about Musa's accidental killing challenge your default reaction?

The Ordeal of Prophet Sulayman: A Lesson in Mindfulness
Sanusi explains the trial of Sulayman as a reminder, not punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the trial of Prophet Sulayman was a gentle reminder from Allah to cultivate mindfulness, not a punishment for forgetfulness.

Core Idea
Allah's trials of His prophets are reminders, not retributions.

In this passage, Sanusi interprets the Quranic trial of Prophet Sulayman. He emphasizes that the birth of a deformed child after Sulayman forgot to say 'in sha' Allah' was not a punishment, but a loving discipline from Allah. This sets a key principle for understanding prophetic trials: they are educational, not punitive.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Let the author's own wording sink in before analyzing.
Notice the author's strong opening: 'As for the saying...'
2
Identify the incident
Find what exactly the trial consisted of: Sulayman forgot to say 'in sha' Allah' while vowing to father many warriors.
The hadith source is provided in the footnote.
3
Grasp the key distinction
Notice that Sanusi explicitly denies this was a punishment ('that was not a punishment') and calls it a 'reminder' (tanbih). This is the core teaching.
Contrast this with common assumptions about divine trials.
4
Appreciate the honor of direct discipline
Reflect on the phrase: Allah Himself undertook their discipline, not through ordinary means. This shows His care for the prophets.
The casting of the half-child on the throne is for reflection.
5
Heed the warning
Note the author's strong warning against listening to ignorant historians and exegetes who narrate 'grave matters' about this event.
This reminds us to rely on sound scholarly interpretations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قولُه تبارك وتعالى : ﴿ وَلَقَدْ فَتَنَّا سُلَيْمَنَ ﴾ [صَ : ٣٤] : فمعناه : ابتليناه بولادةِ شِقّ إنسان حينَ نَسِيَ أن يقول : إِنْ شَاءَ الله ، بعد قولِهِ : لأطوفَنَّ الليلة على مئة امرأةٍ أو تسع وتسعين ، كلُهُنَّ يأتين بفارس يجاهد في سبيلِ اللهِ (۱) ، وليس ذلكَ عقوبة ، بل تنبيهاً من المولى تبارك وتعالى لخاصَّتِهِ على كمال التحرُّزِ في المستقبل ، وشرَّفهم جلَّ وعلا بأن تولَّى رياضتهم بنفسِهِ ، ولم يكلْهُم إلى غيرِهِ مِنَ الأسبابِ العادية ، وألقى ذلكَ الشَّقَ على كرسيّهِ لكمال الاعتبار ، وللاعتناء برؤيةِ ما نَبَّهَهُ بهِ المولى العظيمُ عِياناً ، وإِيَّاكَ يا أخي أن تصغي لِمَا يذكره هنا جهلةُ المؤرّخين والمفسرينَ مِنَ العظائم التي لا يُرضى أن يلتفت إليها (۱) رواه البخاري ( ۲۸۱۹ ) من حديث سيدنا أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه .
As for the saying of the Lord, Blessed and Exalted: {And indeed We tried Sulayman} [Sad: 34] - its meaning is: We tested him by the birth of a half-human when he forgot to say 'If Allah wills' after his saying: 'I will surely circumambulate tonight upon one hundred women or ninety-nine, each of them will come with a horseman who fights in the way of Allah' (1). And that was not a punishment, but rather a reminder from the Lord, Blessed and Exalted, for His elect regarding perfect caution in the future. And He, Mighty and Majestic, honored them by undertaking their discipline Himself, and did not entrust them to other than Him from the ordinary causes. And He cast that half-human upon his throne for complete consideration, and for the care of seeing what the Great Lord had alerted him to by direct sight. And beware, O my brother, of listening to what the ignorant historians and exegetes mention here of grave matters that it is not pleasing to pay attention to. (1) Reported by al-Bukhari (2819) from the hadith of our master Abu Hurayra, may Allah be pleased with him.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage interprets the Quranic verse about the trial of Prophet Sulayman. The author explains that the trial was the birth of a deformed child ('half-human') because Sulayman forgot to say 'in sha' Allah' when he vowed to have many children who would be fighters. The author emphasizes that this was not a punishment (uquba) but a reminder (tanbih) from Allah for His elite to be more cautious. Moreover, it was an honor that Allah Himself disciplined them directly rather than through ordinary means. The casting of the deformed child on the throne was for reflection. The author warns against listening to false stories by ignorant historians and exegetes about this event. A footnote provides the hadith source.

Key Terms
فتنة
شق إنسان
إن شاء الله
عقوبة
تنبيه
رياضة
كرسي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Allah punished Prophet Sulayman for forgetting to say 'in sha' Allah'.
Correction: Sanusi explicitly states it was not a punishment but a reminder (tanbih) to cultivate caution, showing Allah's care and honor for His prophets.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what was the purpose of Allah's trial of Prophet Sulayman?
A) To punish him for a sin
B) To alert him to be more cautious in the future
C) To test his patience
D) To demonstrate his power to others

Key Takeaway
The trial of Prophet Sulayman was a loving reminder from Allah to be mindful, not a punishment for forgetfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a recent disappointment or difficulty in your life. Have you been interpreting it as a punishment or as a loving reminder from Allah? What would change in your response if you truly saw it as the latter?
?
When was the last time you made a promise or plan without saying 'In sha Allah'? How can you train yourself to be more mindful of Allah’s will in your daily speech and intentions?
?
Have you ever believed or repeated a story about a prophet that you later found out was weak or fabricated? How will you ensure you only accept authentic narrations about the prophets going forward?

Ibrahim's Didactic Argument Against Star Worship
Sanusi defends Ibrahim's prophethood from the misinterpretation of star worship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Prophet Ibrahim's statement about the star was a didactic argument for his people, not an expression of belief in its divinity nor a sign of doubt.

Core Idea
Ibrahim's words were a proof, not a profession of faith.

This passage addresses a common misunderstanding about Prophet Ibrahim. Some imagine that Ibrahim, upon seeing the stars, genuinely believed they were gods or at least doubted before being guided. Sanusi clarifies that Ibrahim's speech was a method of argumentation, not a statement of belief. The Quran itself calls it a 'proof' given to him. This lesson unpacks that crucial distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Pay attention to the Quranic verses embedded in the text.
2
Identify the two interpretations
The passage contrasts the correct interpretation (didactic argument) with the mistaken one (actual belief or doubt). Highlight the phrases that show this contrast.
Look for the word 'لا' (not) which negates the wrong interpretation.
3
Understand the Quranic confirmation
Sanusi quotes Quran 6:83 to support his view. Reflect on why this verse is decisive evidence that Ibrahim's words were a proof, not a lapse in faith.
The verse calls it 'Our argument which We gave Ibrahim'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قوله جل وعلا في حقٌّ إبراهيم عليه الصلاةُ والسلام : ﴿فَلَمَّا جَنَّ عَلَيْهِ الَّيْلُ رَمَا كَوْكَبَا قَالَ هَذَا رَبِّي ... ﴾ [الأنعام : ٧٦] إلى آخره : فهو إقامة منه عليه الصلاة والسلامُ الدلالة لقومه على حدوث هذهِ العلويَّاتِ التي عبدَها قومُهُ وادَّعَوا لها الألوهيَّةَ ، ولذلك قال جلَّ مِنْ قائل : ﴿ وَتِلْكَ حُجَّتُنَا وَآتَيْنَهَا إِبْرَاهِيمَ عَلَى قَوْمِهِ ... [الأنعام : ٨٣] الآية ، لا أَنَّهُ عليهِ الصلاة والسلام كان يعتقد ربوبيتها أو يشكُ فيها ، وعند إقامة هذا الدليل زالَ عنه ذلك الاعتقاد أوِ الشكُ ! كما توهَّمَهُ
As for the saying of the Mighty and Majestic regarding Ibrahim, peace be upon him: {When the night covered him, he saw a star and said, 'This is my Lord'...} [al-An'am: 76] to the end: it is an establishment from him, peace be upon him, of the proof for his people of the temporality of these celestial bodies which his people worshipped and claimed divinity for them. Therefore the Mighty among speakers said: {And that was Our argument which We gave Ibrahim against his people...} [al-An'am: 83] the verse. It is not that he, peace be upon him, believed in their lordship or doubted in it, and at the establishment of this proof that belief or doubt left him! As some have imagined.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage defends Prophet Ibrahim against the misconception that he actually worshipped the stars. The author explains that Ibrahim's statement 'this is my Lord' was a didactic argument (iqamat al-dalala) for his people to prove that the celestial bodies are created and not gods. The Quran itself confirms this by calling it 'Our argument which We gave Ibrahim'. Therefore, Ibrahim never believed these objects were lords, nor did he doubt monotheism and then later realize the truth. The author rejects the mistaken interpretation that Ibrahim's faith was incomplete or that he was a star-worshipper before prophethood.

Key Terms
إقامة الدلالة
حدوث
علويات
حجة
ربوبية
شك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Prophet Ibrahim actually worshipped celestial bodies before prophethood or was initially uncertain about Allah's oneness.
Correction: Ibrahim's statement was a didactic argument (iqamat al-dalala) to prove the temporality of the stars, moon, and sun, as confirmed by the Quran calling it 'Our argument' given to him. He never believed or doubted their lordship.

Checkpoint
What was Prophet Ibrahim's purpose in saying 'this is my Lord' about the star?
A) He truly believed it was his Lord
B) He was testing his people's reaction
C) He was proving that those objects are created and not gods
D) He was expressing doubt in Allah

Key Takeaway
Ibrahim never believed the stars were lords; his words were a proof of their createdness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How certain are you that Allah alone is your Lord? Do your actions reflect the same unwavering certainty Ibrahim had, or do you sometimes 'worship' other things by prioritizing them over Allah? What step can you take today to align your heart with Ibrahim's tawhid?
?
When you read Quranic verses that seem ambiguous, do you rush to a literal understanding or do you seek the established interpretation of the scholars? Ibrahim's words could have been misunderstood; how do you guard against misinterpreting Allah's book?
?
Imagine someone accuses you of doubting Allah based on your words or actions. Would you be able to defend yourself with the same clarity Sanusi defended Ibrahim? How would you prove that your heart is fixed on tawhid?

The Test of Prophet Solomon: A Reminder, Not a Punishment
Sanusi explains the Quranic test of Solomon and refutes false narratives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct interpretation of the Quranic test of Prophet Solomon and why it was a reminder, not a punishment, preserving prophetic infallibility.

Core Idea
The test of Solomon was a reminder from Allah, not a punishment for sin.

In this passage, Sanusi explains the meaning of the trial of Prophet Solomon mentioned in the Quran. He clarifies that it was not a punishment but a divine reminder to be cautious. He also warns against false historical accounts and reflects on the station of servitude before Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic text of the passage once, then read the literal English translation. Let the words of Sanusi sink in before analyzing.
2
Identify the nature of the test
Notice that the test was the birth of a piece of a human (شق إنسان) because Solomon forgot to say 'if Allah wills'. Understand that this was not a sin but a forgetfulness.
Sanusi emphasizes it was a reminder (تنبيه), not a punishment (عقوبة).
3
Understand the divine purpose
Reflect on why Allah would test a prophet in this way: to train and discipline His elite servants directly, and to teach them complete caution.
4
Heed the warning against false stories
Sanusi explicitly warns against listening to ignorant historians and exegetes who fabricate enormities. This is a crucial guardrail for the student.
This preserves the dignity and infallibility of prophets.
5
Reflect on the concluding principle
The passage ends with a profound observation: even a great scholar's deeds, compared to Allah's majesty, appear as shortcoming requiring forgiveness.
This reinforces the humility of the prophetic station.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا قولُه تبارك وتعالى : ﴿ وَلَقَدْ فَتَنَّا سُلَيْمَنَ ﴾ [صَ : ٣٤] : فمعناه : ابتليناه بولادةِ شِقّ إنسان حينَ نَسِيَ أن يقول : إِنْ شَاءَ الله ، بعد قولِهِ : لأطوفَنَّ الليلة على مئة امرأةٍ أو تسع وتسعين ، كلُهُنَّ يأتين بفارس يجاهد في سبيلِ اللهِ (۱) ، وليس ذلكَ عقوبة ، بل تنبيهاً من المولى تبارك وتعالى لخاصَّتِهِ على كمال التحرُّزِ في المستقبل ، وشرَّفهم جلَّ وعلا بأن تولَّى رياضتهم بنفسِهِ ، ولم يكلْهُم إلى غيرِهِ مِنَ الأسبابِ العادية ، وألقى ذلكَ الشَّقَ على كرسيّهِ لكمال الاعتبار ، وللاعتناء برؤيةِ ما نَبَّهَهُ بهِ المولى العظيمُ عِياناً ، وإِيَّاكَ يا أخي أن تصغي لِمَا يذكره هنا جهلةُ المؤرّخين والمفسرينَ مِنَ العظائم التي لا يُرضى أن يلتفت إليها • مقام كان من مقام العبودية وإن كان عالماً جدّاً . . إذا قوبل ذلك بجلال كبرياء الله تعالى صار عين التقصير الذي يجب منه الاستغفار )
As for His saying, Blessed and Exalted, {And certainly We tried Solomon} [Sad 38:34]: its meaning is: We tested him with the birth of a piece of a human when he forgot to say 'if Allah wills' after his statement: 'I will certainly go around tonight to a hundred or ninety-nine women, each of them will come with a horseman fighting in the way of Allah' (1). And that was not a punishment, but a reminder from the Master, Blessed and Exalted, to His elite of complete caution in the future. And He, Glorious and Exalted, honored them by undertaking their discipline Himself, and did not entrust them to other than Him from ordinary causes. And He cast that piece on his throne for complete consideration and for attention to seeing with one's own eyes what the Great Master had warned him about. And beware, my brother, of listening to what the ignorant historians and exegetes mention here of enormities that it is not pleasing to turn attention to. • It is a station from among the stations of servitude; even though one is very knowledgeable, when compared to the majesty of Allah's greatness, it becomes the essence of shortcoming for which seeking forgiveness is obligatory.)
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is an interpretation of the Quranic verse about the trial of Prophet Solomon. Sanusi begins by explaining the meaning of 'trial' (فتنة) in this context: it refers to the birth of a deformed child (شق إنسان) that occurred because Solomon forgot to say 'if Allah wills' when he swore to consort with many women. Sanusi emphasizes that this was not a punishment (عقوبة) but a reminder (تنبيه) from Allah to His special servants to be perfectly cautious. He then notes that Allah honored the prophets by personally disciplining them without using ordinary causes. He mentions that the piece was placed on Solomon's throne for a lesson. Finally, he warns against listening to false stories fabricated by ignorant historians and exegetes. The passage concludes with a general principle about the station of servitude: even a great scholar, when compared to Allah's majesty, sees himself as deficient and must seek forgiveness.

Key Terms
فتنة (test/trial)
عصمة (infallibility)
شق (piece/miscarriage)
تنبيه (reminder/warning)
رياضة (discipline/training)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Solomon sinned by forgetting to say 'insha'Allah' and was punished.
Correction: Sanusi explicitly says the test was not a punishment but a reminder (تنبيه), and prophets are infallible (عصمة) — they do not commit sins.

Checkpoint
What is the correct interpretation of the 'test' of Prophet Solomon according to Sanusi?
A) Solomon was punished for a sin.
B) Allah tested Solomon by reminding him of future caution.
C) Solomon doubted Allah's power.
D) The test was a sign of Solomon's weakness.

Key Takeaway
The test of Prophet Solomon was a divine reminder to be cautious, not a punishment, and it underscores the infallibility of prophets and the importance of reliance on Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a difficulty or a trial in your life, do you instinctively see it as punishment for a mistake or as a loving reminder from Allah to draw closer to Him? Solomon's test was a reminder of his complete reliance on Allah. What is one trial you are currently facing that could be reinterpreted as a divine reminder? What specific step will you take this week to respond with gratitude rather than frustration?
?
The lesson states that even a very knowledgeable person, when compared to Allah's majesty, sees their actions as 'the essence of shortcoming.' Think of a moment this week when you felt proud of your knowledge or deeds. How did that pride distance you from feeling your need for Allah's forgiveness? Write down one concrete way you will humble yourself today in front of Allah—perhaps by spending extra time in istighfar or by silently serving someone without seeking recognition.
?
Prophet Solomon, despite his immense wisdom and power, was tested over something as simple as a phrase: 'insha'Allah.' What small habits or words in your daily life do you neglect that could be opportunities to remember Allah? Commit to one specific phrase you will start saying consistently this week (e.g., 'insha'Allah' before plans, 'alhamdulillah' after meals, 'astaghfirullah' when you feel pride). How will you remind yourself to keep this commitment?
