The Prophecy of the Mighty One with the Sword
Sanusi interprets a Psalms verse as a prophecy about Prophet Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi interprets Psalms 45:3-5 as a prophecy about Prophet Muhammad's mission and the subjugation of nations.

Core Idea
The Psalms prophesy Muhammad's armed mission to bring all nations under Islam.

Sanusi turns to the Psalms to show that earlier scriptures foretold the coming of Prophet Muhammad. In this passage, he cites a verse describing a 'mighty one' armed with a sword, whose laws inspire awe and whose arrows subdue nations. Sanusi explains that this refers to the Prophet's role in inviting humanity to Islam, with the choice of belief or paying the jizya. This lesson will unpack that interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Psalms citation
Read the Arabic text of the Psalms verse as quoted by Sanusi. Notice the imagery: sword, law, awe, arrows, nations falling.
2
Sanusi's interpretation
Read Sanusi's explanation that this addresses Prophet Muhammad. Understand his gloss on 'falling under you' as entering Islam or paying jizya.
Sanusi connects the sword imagery to the Islamic concept of jizya.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Consider why Sanusi uses this proof: to show that prior scriptures affirm Muhammad's prophethood and the nature of his mission.
This is a samiyyat argument from previous revelations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها : ما جاءَ في الزَّبورِ مِنْ قولِهِ تعالى خطاباً لنبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : ( تَقلَّدْ أيُّها الجبَّارُ السيف ؛ فإنَّ ناموسَكَ وشرائعَكَ مقرونة بهيبة يمينكَ ، وسهامَكَ مسنونةٌ ، والأممَ يَخِرُّونَ تحتك ((١) ؛ أي : يَذِلُّونَ لكَ حتى يدخلوا في الإسلام طوعاً أو كرهاً ، أو يؤدُّوا الجزية عن يد وهم صاغرونَ .
وفي الزَّبورِ أيضاً : يقولُ اللهُ تعالى لداود عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( سيُولَدُ لكَ ولدٌ أُدعى لهُ أباً ، ويُدعى لي ابناً ، فقال داود عليه الصلاةُ والسلام : اللهمَّ ؛ ابعث جاعل السنَّةِ كي يُعَلِّمَ الناسَ أَنَّهُ بشرٌ ((٢) .
(۱) انظر ( سفر المزامير » ( ٣/٤٥ ٥ )
(۲) انظر ( سفر صموئيل الثاني ) ( ١٢/٧ - ١٤ ) .
And among them: what came in the Psalms from His saying, Most High, addressing our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace: "Gird yourself, O mighty one, with the sword; for your law and your statutes are coupled with the awe of your right hand, and your arrows are sharpened, and the nations fall under you." (1) i.e., they will be humbled to you until they enter Islam willingly or unwillingly, or pay the jizya by hand while they are subdued. And in the Psalms also: God Most High says to David, peace and blessings be upon him: "A son will be born to you; I will be called a father to him, and he will be called a son to me." So David, peace and blessings be upon him, said: "O God, send a maker of the Sunnah to teach people that he is a human." (2) (1) See the Book of Psalms, 45:3-5. (2) See the Second Book of Samuel, 12:7-14.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage presents two prophecies from the Psalms (Zabur) that Sanusi interprets as referring to Prophet Muhammad. The first citation is from Psalms 45:3-5, addressing a 'mighty one' with a sword, whose laws are majestic. Sanusi explains that this refers to Muhammad: the nations will be humbled before him, entering Islam or paying jizya. The second citation is from the Psalms (though the footnote identifies it as 2 Samuel 12:7-14), where God tells David that a son will be born to him and will be called a son of God. David responds by praying for 'a maker of the Sunnah' (i.e., Muhammad) to teach people that this son (presumably Jesus) is merely human, countering the Christian claim of divinity. This interpretation uses the Psalms to support prophethood and correct Christian doctrines.

Key Terms
الزبور
الجبَّار
السيف
الجزية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what does the phrase 'the nations fall under you' in Psalms 45:3-5 mean?
A) The nations will be conquered militarily
B) The nations will become Muslims or pay jizya
C) The nations will worship the Prophet
D) The nations will be destroyed

Key Takeaway
Sanusi interprets the Psalms' 'mighty one' as Prophet Muhammad, showing that earlier scriptures prophesied his mission to subdue nations through Islam or jizya.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sanusi interprets the prophecy as nations submitting to the Prophet's sword. Is there any area of your life where you still resist submitting to Allah's command? What would it take for you to 'fall' in humble obedience today?
?
The verse describes two types of acceptance: willingly or by force. When you practice Islam, do you do so with a willing heart or out of compulsion? Pinpoint one act of worship you do reluctantly and commit to changing your intention behind it.
?
The 'mighty one' is armed with a sword of truth. What 'sword' of knowledge or argument have you been given to defend Islam? Are you using it actively, or have you left it sheathed? Write one specific action you will take this week to share or defend the truth.

The Prophecy of the Son and the Maker of the Sunnah
Sanusi interprets a passage from 2 Samuel as a prophecy about Muhammad correcting Christology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi interprets 2 Samuel 12:7-14 as a prophecy about Prophet Muhammad correcting the Christian misunderstanding of Jesus' divine sonship.

Core Idea
David's prayer for a 'maker of the Sunnah' foretells Muhammad's role in clarifying Jesus' humanity.

The second prophecy from the Psalms (actually 2 Samuel) presents a dialogue between God and David about a son to be born. David prays for a 'maker of the Sunnah' to teach people that this son is merely human. Sanusi sees this as a prophecy about Prophet Muhammad, who would come to correct the Christian belief in Jesus' divinity. This lesson examines that interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the second citation
Read the Arabic text: God tells David about a son, and David prays for a maker of the Sunnah. Note the phrase 'maker of the Sunnah'.
2
Understand Sanusi's interpretation
Sanusi interprets this as referring to Prophet Muhammad as the one who teaches that the son (Jesus) is a human being, not divine.
The son referred to is traditionally understood as Solomon, but Sanusi applies it to Jesus.
3
Appreciate the polemical purpose
Consider how this argument refutes Christian claims of Jesus' divinity by showing that even David prayed for someone to clarify Jesus' humanity.
This is an example of using earlier scriptures to support Islamic theology.

Understanding Jesus' Ascension and His Role in Muhammad's Prophethood
Explains Jesus' statement about going to his Father and his sending of Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the metaphorical interpretation of Jesus' ascension to his Lord and the two possible meanings of his sending the Prophet Muhammad.

Core Idea
Jesus' 'going to the Father' is spiritual ascent; his sending Muhammad is either intercession or prophecy sign.

This passage from Sanusi's commentary clarifies two expressions from Islamic tradition: Jesus' statement about going to his Father and his reference to sending a prophet after him. These phrases might seem confusing if taken literally, but Sanusi provides a metaphorical and theological explanation grounded in the context of prophethood. Let's explore how he unpacks each one.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to get a clear picture of what Sanusi is explaining.
Notice the two distinct topics: Jesus' ascension and his sending of Muhammad.
2
Understand the first part: Jesus' ascension
Notice how 'Father' is explained as 'his Lord' and 'departure' is not a physical travel but elevation to a place of honor and spiritual retreat from people.
This reframes a potentially confusing phrase in a metaphorical light.
3
Analyze the two interpretations of Jesus sending Muhammad
Identify the two possibilities: (1) Jesus actively intercedes with Allah for Muhammad's sending, or (2) Jesus knew his ascension would be a sign of Muhammad's prophethood, so he metaphorically attributed the sending to himself.
Both interpretations avoid attributing literal agency to Jesus over Allah's decree.
4
Reflect on metaphorical language
Consider why Sanusi uses the term 'metaphor' for the second interpretation. How does this preserve theological principles while explaining the hadith?
Metaphorical interpretation is a key tool in Islamic theology to harmonize texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومعنى انطلاقِ عيسى عليهِ السلامُ إلى أبيه ؛ أي : ربِّهِ عزَّ وجلَّ : انطلاقه إلى محلّ رفعتِهِ وكرامتِهِ ، والاستراحةُ مِنَ الناسِ ، والتوجه بكُليَّةِ القلبِ إلى المولى تبارك وتعالى ، وكونه يرسل نبينا صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : يحتمل أن يكون معناه : أَنَّهُ يَتسبب في ذلكَ برغبتِهِ إلى الله تعالى ، ويحتملُ أنْ يكونَ : لمَّا عَلِمَ عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ أَنَّ بعْثَ سيّدِنا ومولانا محمَّدٍ صلى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ إِنَّما يكون بعد رفعه وتغييبِهِ مِنَ الناسِ ، وأنَّ رفعَهُ مِنْ أماراتِ بعثِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ. . فأسند إرساله إلى نفسه بهذا المعنى على سبيل المجاز ، والله تعالى أعلم.
And the meaning of Jesus's, peace be upon him, departure to his Father – i.e., his Lord, Mighty and Majestic – is his departure to the place of his elevation and honor, and seeking rest from people, and turning with the entirety of the heart to the Lord, Blessed and Exalted. And his sending our Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace: it is possible that its meaning is that he causes that by his desire to Allah Almighty, and it is possible that it is: since he, peace and blessings be upon him, knew that the sending of our Master and Lord Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, would only be after his (Jesus's) elevation and concealment from people, and that his elevation is among the signs of his (Muhammad's) sending. So he attributed the sending to himself in this sense metaphorically. And Allah Almighty knows best.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory commentary on the meaning of Jesus's statement about going to his Father, which is reported in Islamic tradition. The author first clarifies that 'Father' here means his Lord, metaphorically, and that going to him means being raised to a place of honor and spiritual retreat. Then he discusses the phrase 'he sends our Prophet,' referring to Jesus sending Muhammad. He presents two possible interpretations: first, that Jesus intercedes with Allah for Muhammad's sending; second, that Jesus knew that Muhammad's mission would occur after his own ascension, which is a sign of that mission, so he metaphorically attributed the sending to himself. The passage concludes by deferring ultimate knowledge to Allah.

Key Terms
انطلاق
رفعة
تغييب
أمارات
بعثة
مجاز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think Jesus' 'going to his Father' implies a physical departure from earth to God.
Correction: It is explained as being raised to a place of honor and spiritual retreat, not a literal journey to God.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many possible meanings are given for Jesus sending our Prophet Muhammad?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
Jesus' ascension is a spiritual elevation, and his role in Muhammad's prophethood is understood either as intercession or as a prophetic sign, both metaphorical.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Jesus 'goes to his Father' means turning entirely to God, have you ever considered that your own spiritual retreats are not about leaving people but about orienting your heart fully toward Him? What would it take for you to make that your daily reality?
?
If Jesus' ascension is a sign of Muhammad's prophethood, do you truly live as if every event in history points to the Prophet's message? How does that change how you see your own life's events?
?
The passage offers two interpretations of Jesus sending Muhammad. Which one challenges your assumptions more: that Jesus interceded for us, or that it is all a metaphor? Are you willing to accept that your understanding of prophethood might need to be more humble and open to Allah's wisdom?

Proof from Psalms: The Mighty One with the Sword
Quotes a Psalm verse as a proof for Muhammad's prophethood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a Psalm verse is interpreted as a prophecy of Prophet Muhammad's mission and authority.

Core Idea
A Psalm verse foretells the Prophet's military and legislative authority.

This passage presents a proof from the Psalms (Zabur), showing that earlier scriptures pointed to the coming of Prophet Muhammad. The author cites a verse describing a mighty figure with a sword and explains it as a prophecy of the Islamic shariah and the universal spread of Islam, either through conversion or submission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the meaning.
The verse is from Psalms 45:3–5, interpreted here as addressing Prophet Muhammad.
2
Identify key terms
Look at the key terms listed: الزبور, الناموس, الشرائع, الجزية, صاغرون. Understand their meanings in context.
الناموس refers to divine law, and الشرائع to revealed statutes.
3
Understand the interpretation
The author explains that 'the nations fall beneath you' means they will be humbled into accepting Islam willingly or by force, or paying jizya in submission.
This interpretation links the verse directly to Muhammad's prophethood.
4
Reflect on the proof's purpose
Consider why this passage is included: it shows that previous scriptures contained prophecies about Muhammad, strengthening the case for his prophethood.
This is part of a broader set of proofs from earlier scriptures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها : ما جاءَ في الزَّبورِ مِنْ قولِهِ تعالى خطاباً لنبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : ( تَقلَّدْ أيُّها الجبَّارُ السيف ؛ فإنَّ ناموسَكَ وشرائعَكَ مقرونة بهيبة يمينكَ ، وسهامَكَ مسنونةٌ ، والأممَ يَخِرُّونَ تحتك((۱) ؛ أي : يَذِلُّونَ لكَ حتى يدخلوا في الإسلام طوعاً أو كرهاً ، أو يؤدُّوا الجزية عن يد وهم صاغرونَ .
And among them: what came in the Psalms (Zabur) from His saying, Almighty, addressing our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace: 'Gird on the sword, O mighty one; for your law and your statutes are coupled with the awe of your right hand, and your arrows are sharpened, and the nations fall beneath you' – i.e., they will be humbled before you until they enter Islam willingly or unwillingly, or pay the jizya from hand while they are subdued.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage presents a proof from the Psalms (Zabur) for the prophethood of Muhammad. The author cites a verse that, in his interpretation, directly addresses Muhammad. The verse describes a mighty figure who is commanded to gird on his sword, indicating military authority. The 'law' and 'statutes' refer to the Islamic shariah, coupled with divine awe. The nations falling beneath him signifies the universal spread of Islam, either through conversion or by paying the jizya in a state of submission. The author explicitly interprets the verse as referring to Muhammad, peace be upon him.

Key Terms
الزبور
الناموس
الشرائع
الجزية
صاغرون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think this Psalm refers to a Hebrew king or the Messiah.
Correction: The author insists it is a prophecy of Muhammad's military and legal authority, based on the description of a law and statutes coupled with awe, and the nations falling beneath him, which matches the spread of Islam.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does 'the nations fall beneath you' mean?
A) They will be destroyed
B) They will be humbled and either accept Islam or pay jizya
C) They will become slaves
D) They will flee

Key Takeaway
The Psalms contain a prophecy of Prophet Muhammad's authority and the universal spread of Islam through conversion or submission.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly accept that this Psalm is a prophecy about Muhammad, then what does it mean for your own submission to his authority? Are there areas of your life where you still resist his law and statutes mentioned in this verse? What will you change this week to bring your life fully under his guidance?
?
The verse declares that nations will fall beneath the Prophet — a promise of ultimate victory. In moments when you see the Ummah weak or divided, does this prophecy strengthen your trust in Allah's plan? What is one concrete step you can take to help fulfil this prophecy in your own sphere of influence?
?
'Willingly or unwillingly' describes how people submit. Think about your own heart: Do you submit to Allah's messenger willingly in every aspect of your faith, or is there a part where you resist? Ask yourself honestly: what would it take for you to surrender completely to the 'law and statutes' that come with awe?

Psalm Prophecy: Jesus and the Establisher of Sunnah
Quotes a Psalm about a son born to David (Jesus) and the one who later establishes the Sunnah (Muhammad).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Psalms are used to affirm the prophethood of Muhammad and to refute misconceptions about Jesus and the nature of Allah.

Core Idea
The Psalms foretell Jesus and Muhammad; Muhammad clarifies Jesus's true servanthood.

The author presents another proof from the Psalms, quoting a divine address to David. This passage not only identifies the prophesied son as Jesus but also highlights Muhammad's role as the one who would clarify Jesus's humanity and Allah's oneness. Let's read the source and unpack its layers.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and Translation
First, read the Arabic passage slowly. Then read the literal translation to grasp the narrative.
Notice the dialogue between God and David.
2
Identify Key Figures
Identify the son born to David (Jesus) and the 'establisher of the Sunnah' (Muhammad). Note David's prayer requesting this figure.
The son is not Muhammad but Jesus.
3
Understand Muhammad's Mission
See how Muhammad is described with three titles: establisher of Sunnah, extinguisher of innovation, and remover of distress. Reflect on his role in correcting beliefs.
4
Analyze the Theological Correction
Look at the teachings Muhammad brought: Jesus is a servant, Allah does not take a son, and Allah is One and Self-Sufficient.
This refutes Christian doctrines.
5
Connect to the Proof
Consider how this Psalm serves as evidence for Muhammad's prophethood and the truth of Islamic teachings about Jesus.
The passage uses earlier scripture to support later revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الزَّبورِ أيضاً : يقولُ اللهُ تعالى لداود عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( سيُولَدُ لكَ ولدٌ أُدعى لهُ أباً ، ويُدعى لي ابناً ، فقال داود عليه الصلاةُ والسلام : اللهمَّ ؛ ابعث جاعل السنَّةِ كي يُعَلِّمَ الناسَ أَنَّهُ بشرٌ ((٢) . وهذا الولد الذي وُلِدَ لداودَ عليه الصلاةُ والسلام بهذه الصفة المذكورة هو عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام ، ولم يبعث الله تعالى بعدَهُ جاعلاً للسنة وخامداً للبدعة وكاشفاً للغُمَّةِ . . إلا نبيَّنا ومولانا محمداً صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، فأعلمَ الناسَ أنَّ عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام عبد الله ورسوله ، وأَنَّهُ لن يَستنكِفَ المسيح أن يكون عبداً للهِ ولا الملائكة المقربونَ ، وأَنَّهُ ما كانَ اللهِ أَنْ يَتَّخِذَ ولداً ، إِنْ كُلُّ مَنْ فِي السماوات والأرض إلا أتي الرحمن عبداً ، وأن مولانا جل وعزَّ أحدٌ صمد ، لم يلد ولم يولد ، ولم يكن لهُ كُفُواً أحدٌ .
And in the Psalms also: Allah Almighty says to David, peace and blessings be upon him: 'A son will be born to you; I will be called a father to him, and he will be called a son to Me.' So David, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'O Allah, send the establisher of the Sunnah so that he may teach the people that he (the son) is a human.' And this son who was born to David, peace and blessings be upon him, with this described attribute is Jesus, peace and blessings be upon him. And Allah Almighty did not send after him an establisher of the Sunnah, extinguisher of innovation, and revealer of distress except our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. So he taught the people that Jesus, peace and blessings be upon him, is the servant of Allah and His Messenger, and that the Messiah would never disdain to be a servant of Allah, nor the angels who are near, and that it is not for Allah to take a son; there is none in the heavens and the earth but comes to the Most Merciful as a servant. And that our Master, Mighty and Majestic, is One, Self-Sufficient; He does not beget nor was He begotten, and there is none comparable to Him.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage provides another proof from the Psalms. It quotes a conversation where God tells David that a son will be born to him, and David prays for the sending of an 'establisher of the Sunnah' to clarify that the son is human. The author identifies this son as Jesus. Then he states that after Jesus, no one was sent with the role of establishing the Sunnah, extinguishing innovation, and removing distress except Muhammad. Muhammad then taught the people the correct belief about Jesus: that he is a servant and messenger, not divine, and that Allah is transcendently one and free from offspring. The passage thus uses the Psalms to affirm Muhammad's prophethood and to refute Christian doctrines about Jesus.

Key Terms
الزبور
داود
جاعل السنة
خامد البدعة
كاشف الغمة
عبد
أحد صمد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the son born to David is Prophet Muhammad.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that the son is Jesus, and Muhammad is the one sent later to correct misunderstandings about that son.

Checkpoint
What did David ask Allah to send?
A) The Messiah
B) The establisher of the Sunnah
C) A prophet like Moses
D) A king

Key Takeaway
The Psalms contain prophecies that point to Jesus and Muhammad, and Muhammad's mission was to correct the understanding of Jesus's nature and Allah's oneness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
David prayed for someone to teach people that Jesus is merely human. When you look at your own understanding of Jesus, is there any residue of belief that elevates him beyond servanthood? How will you actively correct that in your heart today?
?
The Psalm used language that could be misconstrued as divine sonship. Are there any verses in your own scripture or traditions that you have misinterpreted? What step will you take to seek the correct understanding from this lesson's approach?
?
Muhammad's mission was to clarify and correct. In what area of your life are you most in need of a 'clarifier'—someone or something to remove confusion? Will you seek the Sunnah as that guide, starting today?

The Servant in Isaiah's Prophecy
Isaiah quotes God describing His servant's qualities and miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the prophecy of Isaiah describes Prophet Muhammad's character, miracles, and the name Ahmad.

Core Idea
Isaiah foretold a gentle servant who works spiritual miracles and is named Ahmad.

This lesson explores a prophecy from the Book of Isaiah that Muslims interpret as referring to Prophet Muhammad. The passage describes a servant chosen by God, his gentle manner, his miraculous deeds, and even mentions the name 'Ahmad'. As you read, notice how these details align with the life and mission of Muhammad as understood in Islamic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the prophecy
Start by reading the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the flow: God introduces His servant, then describes his actions and character.
2
Identify key traits
Look for the traits mentioned: the servant does not laugh loudly, his voice is not heard in markets, he performs miracles like opening blind eyes and reviving hearts.
These traits reflect Muhammad's known gentleness and spiritual impact.
3
Find the name Ahmad
Pay attention to the explicit mention of 'Ahmad' in the prophecy. That is one of the names of the Prophet Muhammad.
This is a strong direct reference.
4
Understand the miracles
Consider the miracles: opening blind eyes, making deaf hear, reviving sealed hearts. While literal interpretations exist, scholars often see these as spiritual healings.
Compare this with the Quranic description of Muhammad's mission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال إشعياءُ النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام عن الله تعالى : ( عبدي الذي سُرَّتْ بهِ نفسي ، أُنزِلُ عليهِ وحيي ، فيظهر في الأمم عدلي يوصي الأمم بالوصايا ، لا يضحك ولا يُسمع صوتُهُ في الأسواق ، يفتحُ العيونَ العُورَ ، ويُسْمِعُ الآذانَ الصُّمَّ ، ويحيي القلوب الغُلْفَ ، وما أعطيهِ لا أعطيه غيرَهُ ، أحمدُ يَحمَدُ الله حمداً ) ثمَّ أشار إلى بلدِهِ العطشى مكَّةَ فقال : ( تفرَحُ البرية العطشى ، وسُكَانُها يُهللونَ الله تعالى على كلِّ شَرَفٍ ، ويُكبّرونَهُ على كل رابيةٍ ، لا يَضعُفُ ولا يُغلَبُ ، ولا يميل إلى الهوى ، ولا يُسمَعُ في الأسواقِ صوتُهُ ، ولا يُذِلُّ الصالحين الذين هم كالقصبة الضعيفة ، بل يُقوّي الصادقين ، وهو رُكُنُ للمتواضعين ، وهو نورُ اللهِ الذي لا يُطفَأُ )
And Isaiah the prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, said about Allah Almighty: 'My servant in whom My soul delights; I send down My revelation upon him; he will manifest My justice among the nations; he commands the nations with the commandments; he does not laugh nor is his voice heard in the markets; he opens blind eyes, makes deaf ears hear, revives sealed hearts; and what I give him I do not give to other than him. Ahmad praises God with praise.' Then he pointed to his thirsty land, Mecca, and said: 'The thirsty wilderness rejoices, and its inhabitants glorify Allah on every height and magnify Him on every hill; he does not weaken nor is he overcome; he does not incline to desire; his voice is not heard in the markets; he does not humiliate the righteous who are like a weak reed, but strengthens the truthful; he is a support for the humble; and he is the light of Allah that is never extinguished.'
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage presents a prophecy from Isaiah, which the author interprets as referring to Prophet Muhammad. It begins by describing a servant chosen by God, upon whom revelation is sent. He will establish justice and give commandments. Notable characteristics: he does not laugh (or is not loud in laughter), his voice is not raised in markets (indicating gentleness), he performs miracles: opening blind eyes, making the deaf hear, reviving sealed hearts (spiritual healing). The name 'Ahmad' is explicitly mentioned in the prophecy, which is one of the names of Muhammad. Then the prophecy shifts to describe the land of Mecca as a thirsty wilderness that will rejoice, with people praising God on every height – a reference to the Islamic call to prayer (takbir) on hills. The servant is described as steadfast, not weak, not vain, not humiliating the weak but strengthening the truthful, and being a support for the humble. He is called the light of Allah that cannot be extinguished. This passage thus uses Isaiah to affirm Muhammad's prophethood, his character, and the location of his mission.

Key Terms
إشعياء
عبدي
الوصايا
العيون العور
الآذان الصم
القلوب الغلف
أحمد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the miracles refer only to physical healings by Jesus.
Correction: The prophecy is about God's servant who is named Ahmad, and the miracles include reviving sealed hearts, which aligns with Muhammad's spiritual mission.

Checkpoint
What does the prophecy say about the servant's voice in the markets?
A) It is loud and clear
B) It is not heard
C) It is heard in the temple
D) It is like thunder

Key Takeaway
Isaiah foretells a gentle servant named Ahmad who will perform spiritual miracles and receive a unique revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Has your heart become sealed to the Quran's guidance? What specific habit of neglect or sin has deadened your spiritual hearing, and what will you do this week to reopen your ears to Allah's revelation?
?
The servant was gentle—his voice was not raised in markets. When you speak about your faith, are you loud, argumentative, or proud? Think of one recent conversation where you could have been more gentle like the servant, and commit to changing that tomorrow.
?
God gave His servant a unique revelation not given to others. Do you truly thank Allah for sending Muhammad with the Quran, or do you take it for granted? Write down one concrete way you will honor that unique gift starting today.

Mecca and the Light of Allah
Isaiah describes the land of Mecca and the servant's enduring light.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Isaiah's prophecy describes the land of Mecca and the servant's role as a support for the humble and an inextinguishable light.

Core Idea
Isaiah foretells that Mecca will rejoice and its people will praise God, and the servant will be a lasting light.

In the second part of the Isaiah prophecy, the focus shifts to the 'thirsty land' of Mecca. The prophecy describes joy and worship in that land, and further attributes of the servant: he does not weaken, he does not humiliate the weak, he strengthens the truthful, and he is a support for the humble. Finally, he is called the light of Allah that is never extinguished. This lesson unpacks these descriptions and their connection to Prophet Muhammad's mission in Mecca.

Guided Path
1
Read the prophecy about the land
Read the Arabic: 'تفرَحُ البرية العطشى' and the surrounding text. Note the reference to 'barriyah 'atsha' (thirsty wilderness) which is identified as Mecca.
This is a symbolic reference to a barren land that becomes joyful.
2
Observe the acts of worship
The inhabitants glorify and magnify Allah on every height and hill. This is often interpreted as the call to prayer (takbir) on the hills of Mecca.
3
Study the servant's attributes
The servant is described as not weakening, not overcome, not inclining to desire, and not humiliating the righteous but strengthening them. He is a support for the humble.
These reflect the character of the Prophet in dealing with people.
4
Understand the final metaphor
The servant is called 'the light of Allah that is never extinguished' – signifying the permanence of his message and guidance.
Compare with Quranic verses about the light of Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال إشعياءُ النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام عن الله تعالى : ( عبدي الذي سُرَّتْ بهِ نفسي ، أُنزِلُ عليهِ وحيي ، فيظهر في الأمم عدلي يوصي الأمم بالوصايا ، لا يضحك ولا يُسمع صوتُهُ في الأسواق ، يفتحُ العيونَ العُورَ ، ويُسْمِعُ الآذانَ الصُّمَّ ، ويحيي القلوب الغُلْفَ ، وما أعطيهِ لا أعطيه غيرَهُ ، أحمدُ يَحمَدُ الله حمداً ) ثمَّ أشار إلى بلدِهِ العطشى مكَّةَ فقال : ( تفرَحُ البرية العطشى ، وسُكَانُها يُهللونَ الله تعالى على كلِّ شَرَفٍ ، ويُكبّرونَهُ على كل رابيةٍ ، لا يَضعُفُ ولا يُغلَبُ ، ولا يميل إلى الهوى ، ولا يُسمَعُ في الأسواقِ صوتُهُ ، ولا يُذِلُّ الصالحين الذين هم كالقصبة الضعيفة ، بل يُقوّي الصادقين ، وهو رُكُنُ للمتواضعين ، وهو نورُ اللهِ الذي لا يُطفَأُ )

Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage presents a prophecy from Isaiah, which the author interprets as referring to Prophet Muhammad. It begins by describing a servant chosen by God, upon whom revelation is sent. He will establish justice and give commandments. Notable characteristics: he does not laugh (or is not loud in laughter), his voice is not raised in markets (indicating gentleness), he performs miracles: opening blind eyes, making the deaf hear, reviving sealed hearts (spiritual healing). The name 'Ahmad' is explicitly mentioned in the prophecy, which is one of the names of Muhammad. How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The servant does not humiliate the weak but strengthens the truthful. Think of the last time you encountered someone weaker than you—did you lift them up or subtly put them down? What will you do today to be a support for the humble?
?
You are called to be a light that never extinguishes. But when your desires, reputation, or comfort are on the line, does your light flicker? What one desire do you need to stop inclining to so that Allah's light can shine through you without hindrance?

Prophecies of Muhammad in Isaiah
Author cites Isaiah prophecies and interprets them as referring to Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author of the Sanusi commentary uses two prophecies from the Book of Isaiah to prove that the Prophet Muhammad (PBUH) was foretold in earlier scriptures, with explicit references to his name 'Ahmad' and his birthplace Makkah.

Core Idea
Isaiah foretold the coming of Ahmad and the rejoicing of Makkah.

In this passage, al-Sanusi argues that the Prophet Muhammad was prophesied in the Book of Isaiah. He first clarifies that after Jesus, only Muhammad was sent to revive the Sunnah and remove distress. He then presents two prophetic passages from Isaiah that he interprets as describing Muhammad's universal mission, his name 'Ahmad', and the barren land of Makkah that would be blessed by his arrival. This lesson will guide you through these prophecies and the author's reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the background context
Start with the opening lines that establish Jesus as a servant of Allah and state that after him only Muhammad came to revive the Sunnah. This sets the stage for why the prophecies point to Muhammad.
2
Examine the first Isaiah prophecy
Read the first prophecy quoted from Isaiah. Notice the attributes: universal instruction, opening blind eyes and deaf ears, and the name 'Ahmad'. These are key indicators the author will use.
The prophecy includes a description of the desert rejoicing, which the author later connects to Makkah.
3
Study the author's commentary on the first prophecy
The author highlights three pieces of evidence: the phrase 'he will instruct the nations' indicates a universal mission unique to Muhammad; the explicit mention of 'Ahmad'; and the description of the thirsty wilderness as a reference to Makkah.
Notice how each piece is carefully argued from the text.
4
Examine the second Isaiah prophecy
Read the second prophecy which again names 'Ahmad' and describes the desert rejoicing. The author uses this to reinforce the first prophecy and connect it directly to Makkah's blessedness due to the Prophet.
5
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how the author builds his case: clear naming, universal scope, and geographical description. These together form a strong demonstration that Muhammad was foretold in Isaiah.

ولا يُخصم حتى توراته ينقاد الحق ((۱)
فانظُرْ رحمَكَ الله إلى هذا التصريح العظيم بنبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ مِنْ غيرِ ما وجه ؛ كقوله : ( يوصي الأممَ ) فَإِنَّهُ يقتضي البعثَ لجميعِهم ، ولم يثبت ذلكَ إلا لنبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، وقوله : ( أحمدُ يَحمَدُ ) فهذا تصريح باسمِهِ وقوله : ( تفرحُ البرية العطشى ، وسُكَانُها ... ) إلى آخرِهِ : فَإِنَّهُ لا خفاءَ أنَّ هذه أوصافُ مكَّةَ .
وفي صحفِ إشعياء عليه السلام : ( لتفرح أهل البادية العطشى ولتبتهج البراري والفلواتُ ؛ لأنَّها ستعطى بأحمد محاسنَ لبنان وكمثل حسن الدساكير والرياض ((٢)
فانظر أيضاً إلى هذا التصريح الواضح باسمه عليه الصلاة والسلام ، وبما أكرمَ اللهُ تعالى بهِ بلدَهُ مكَّةَ بسبب بركة وجوده ونشأته فيها ، وبعثه منها ، ومعنى كونها عطشى ؛ أي : مِنَ الرُّسُلِ والأنبياء عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام ؛ فإنَّ بلد معظمهم الشام ، فأعطى اللهُ سبحانَهُ لمكة ببعث أشرف الخلق منها صلّى الله عليه وسلَّمَ
And this child who was born to David (peace be upon him) with this described attribute is Jesus (peace be upon him). And Allah Almighty sent after him no one who establishes the Sunnah, extinguishes innovation, and removes distress except our Prophet and master Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace). So he informed the people that Jesus (peace be upon him) is the servant of Allah and His messenger, and that the Messiah would not disdain to be a servant of Allah, nor the angels who are near, and that it is not for Allah to take a son; all who are in the heavens and the earth come to the Most Merciful as servants. And that our Master, Mighty and Majestic, is One, Eternal, He does not give birth nor was He born, and there is none comparable to Him. He is born? And Isaiah the prophet (peace be upon him) said concerning Allah Almighty: (My servant in whom my soul delights; I will send down my revelation upon him, and he will manifest my justice among the nations; he will instruct the nations with commandments; he will not laugh nor will his voice be heard in the markets; he will open blind eyes, and make deaf ears hear, and give life; and what I give him I will not give to another. Ahmad, he will praise Allah with praise.) The hearts the veiled? Then he pointed to his thirsty land, Makkah, and said: (The thirsty wilderness will rejoice, and its inhabitants will glorify Allah on every hill, and magnify Him on every high place; he will not weaken nor be overcome, nor incline to desire, nor will his voice be heard in the markets; nor will he humiliate the righteous who are like a weak reed; rather, he will strengthen the truthful, and he is a support for the humble, and he is the light of Allah that cannot be extinguished. And he will spread my proof in the earth, and the excuse will be cut off by him, and submission until his Torah? the truth will yield.) So look, may Allah have mercy on you, at this great explicit mention of our Prophet and master Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) in more than one way: such as his saying (he will instruct the nations) for it necessitates being sent to all of them, and that has not been established except for our Prophet and master Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace); and his saying (Ahmad, he will praise) this is an explicit mention of his name; and his saying (the thirsty wilderness will rejoice, and its inhabitants...) to the end: for it is not hidden that these are descriptions of Makkah. And in the scriptures of Isaiah (peace be upon him): (Let the thirsty desert dwellers rejoice, and let the wilderness and wastelands be glad; for they will be given through Ahmad the beauties of Lebanon and like the beauty of villages and meadows.) So also look at this clear explicit mention of his name (peace be upon him), and with what Allah Almighty honored his city Makkah due to the blessing of his existence and upbringing in it, and his being sent from it, and the meaning of its being thirsty: i.e., of messengers and prophets (peace be upon them); for the land of most of them is Syria, so Allah Almighty gave Makkah by sending the noblest of creation from it, may Allah bless him and grant him peace.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is a proof from previous scriptures (the Book of Isaiah) for the prophethood of Muhammad (PBUH). The author begins by establishing that Jesus was born miraculously but was a servant and messenger, and that after him only Muhammad came as the one who revives the Sunnah and removes distress. Then the author quotes two prophecies from Isaiah. The first prophecy describes a servant of Allah who will be sent to the nations, open blind eyes, make deaf hear, and is called 'Ahmad'—which is a name of the Prophet. The author points out that the phrase 'he will instruct the nations' indicates a universal mission, which applies only to Muhammad. The second prophecy describes a thirsty land that will rejoice, and its inhabitants glorifying Allah on every hill—clearly referring to Makkah, which was dry of prophets before Muhammad. Then the author cites another passage from Isaiah naming 'Ahmad' again and describing how Makkah will be blessed with 'the beauties of Lebanon' etc. The author concludes by noting that these explicit references show the honor of Makkah because of the Prophet's birth and mission from it.

Key Terms
إشعياء
أحمد
مكة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that biblical prophecies about a coming prophet do not apply to Muhammad.
Correction: This passage shows explicit references to the name 'Ahmad' and descriptions of Makkah, which the author argues can only refer to Muhammad.

Checkpoint
According to the author, which phrase from Isaiah proves that the prophesied prophet was sent to all nations?
A) 'Ahmad, he will praise Allah'
B) 'He will instruct the nations'
C) 'The thirsty wilderness will rejoice'
D) 'He will open blind eyes'

Key Takeaway
These prophecies from Isaiah explicitly foretell Muhammad by name and place of origin, affirming that his coming was known in earlier scriptures.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The source says that the coming of the Prophet Muhammad (PBUH) was foretold in scriptures known to Jews and Christians. Does this challenge you to take the message of the Qur'an more seriously in your own life? What would change if you truly believed that Allah's plan has always been consistent across time?
?
If the name 'Ahmad' was written in the Book of Isaiah, then the coming of our Prophet was not an afterthought—it was part of Allah's plan from the beginning. How does knowing that this revelation was awaited by previous communities affect your gratitude for being born into this ummah? What responsibility does that place on you to live according to his Sunnah?
?
Look at the descriptions of the Prophet in the prophecy: he is described as one who will not humiliate the weak but strengthen them. In your daily interactions, are you a source of strength and support for the vulnerable, or do you overlook them? What specific step can you take this week to emulate the Prophet's mercy as highlighted in this prophecy?

The First Isaiah Prophecy: Universal Mission and the Name 'Ahmad'
First Isaiah prophecy and its three indicators.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a prophecy from Isaiah explicitly points to Prophet Muhammad's universal prophethood and his name.

Core Idea
Isaiah's prophecy explicitly names 'Ahmad' as the universal prophet.

This lesson examines the first of several prophecies from the Old Testament that the author presents as clear declarations of Muhammad's prophethood. The opening prophecy from Isaiah contains multiple specific references to the Prophet's mission and name.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage from 'ولا يخصم' to 'أوصاف مكة' along with its translation. Notice the structure: the author quotes a prophecy and then comments on three aspects.
The prophecy includes the phrase 'Ahmad will praise' which is a direct name.
2
Identify the three indicators
The author points out three things: the phrase 'He will give commandments to the nations' indicating universal mission, 'Ahmad will praise' as a name, and the description of the thirsty wilderness as Mecca.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why the author emphasizes these as 'great declarations' – they are presented as undeniable proofs from previous scriptures.
This connects to the broader argument for Muhammad's prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يُخصم حتى توراته ينقاد الحق ((۱)
فانظُرْ رحمَكَ الله إلى هذا التصريح العظيم بنبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ مِنْ غيرِ ما وجه؛ كقوله : ( يوصي الأممَ ) فإِنَّهُ يقتضي البعثَ لجميعِهم، ولم يثبت ذلكَ إلا لنبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ، وقوله : ( أحمدُ يَحمَدُ ) فهذا تصريح باسمِهِ وقوله : ( تفرحُ البرية العطشى، وسُكَانُها ... ) إلى آخرِهِ : فَإِنَّهُ لا خفاءَ أنَّ هذه أوصافُ مكَّةَ.
وفي صحفِ إشعياء عليه السلام : ( لتفرح أهل البادية العطشى ولتبتهج البراري والفلواتُ؛ لأنَّها ستعطى بأحمد محاسنَ لبنان وكمثل حسن الدساكير والرياض ((٢)
فانظر أيضاً إلى هذا التصريح الواضح باسمه عليه الصلاة والسلام، وبما أكرمَ اللهُ تعالى بهِ بلدَهُ مكَّةَ بسبب بركة وجوده ونشأته فيها، وبعثه منها، ومعنى كونها عطشى؛ أي : مِنَ الرُّسُلِ والأنبياء عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام؛ فإنَّ بلد معظمهم الشام، فأعطى اللهُ سبحانَهُ لمكة ببعث أشرف الخلق منها صلّى الله عليه وسلَّمَ محاسنَ لبنان؛ أي : الشامِ؛ لأنَّ لُبنانَ مِنْ جَبَالِهِ
وفي صُحُفِ إشعياء أيضاً عليهِ السلامُ : ( أَتَتْ أيام الافتقادِ، أَتَتْ أيامُ الكمال )، ثمَّ قال : ( لتعلموا يا بني إسرائيل الجاهلين : أنَّ الذي تُسَمُّونَهُ ضالاً هو صاحب النبوَّةِ، تَفتَرُونَ ذلكَ؛ على كثرة ذنوبكم وعظم فجوركم ((١)
وفي صُحُفِ حزقيال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام، يقولُ عن الله عزّ وجلَّ بعدما ذكر معاصي بني إسرائيل وشبههم بكَرْمةٍ؛ وهي شجرةُ العنب، قال : ( لم تلبث تلكَ الكَرْمَةُ أنْ قُلِعَتْ بالسَّخْطَةِ، ورُمِيَ بها على الأرض، وأحرقتِ السمائمُ ثمارها(٢) ، فعند ذلكَ غُرِسَ غرس في البدو، وفي الأرضِ المهملة العطشى، وخرجَتْ مِنْ أغصانها الفاضلة نار أكلَتْ تلكَ الكَرْمةَ، حتى لم يُوجَد فيها غُصْنُ قوي ولا قضيب ((٣) .
فاعتبر رحمَكَ اللهُ هذا التصريح العظيمَ بهِ عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ وبصفة بلدِهِ مكَّةَ، والتصريح بما وقع له صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ مَعَ اليهودِ بني إسرائيلَ مِنْ تمكينه تعالى له عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ منهم بالقتل الذريع والسبي والإذلالِ لهم بضرب الجزية في جميع بلاد الإسلام .
And he will not be argued down until his Torah leads to the truth. (1) So consider, may Allah have mercy on you, this great declaration concerning our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, from multiple aspects: such as his saying, 'He will give commandments to the nations' – for that necessitates his being sent to all of them, and that has not been established except for our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace; and his saying, 'Ahmad will praise' – this is an explicit mention of his name; and his saying, 'The thirsty wilderness will rejoice, and its inhabitants...' to the end – for it is not hidden that these are descriptions of Mecca. And in the scriptures of Isaiah, peace be upon him: 'Let the thirsty desert dwellers rejoice, and let the barren lands and wildernesses be glad; for they will be given by Ahmad the splendors of Lebanon and like the beauty of villages and meadows.' (2) So look also at this clear declaration of his name, may peace and blessings be upon him, and of what Allah Almighty honored his city Mecca with, due to the blessing of his existence and upbringing therein, and his being sent from it. And the meaning of its being 'thirsty' – i.e., devoid of messengers and prophets, may peace and blessings be upon them; for the land of most of them is Syria. So Allah, glorified be He, gave to Mecca, by sending the most honorable of creation from it, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, the splendors of Lebanon – i.e., Syria; because Lebanon is among its mountains. And in the scriptures of Isaiah also, peace be upon him: 'The days of visitation have come, the days of perfection have come,' then he said: 'Let you know, O ignorant children of Israel, that the one you call a misled person is the owner of prophecy; you falsely accuse him, because of your many sins and great immorality.' (1) And in the scriptures of Ezekiel the prophet, may peace and blessings be upon him, he says about Allah, mighty and majestic, after mentioning the sins of the children of Israel and comparing them to a vine – which is the grapevine – he said: 'That vine did not last; it was pulled up in wrath, and thrown to the ground, and the hot winds burned its fruits. (2) Then at that time, a plant was planted in the desert, in the neglected thirsty land, and from its abundant branches a fire came out and devoured that vine, until no strong branch or rod was found in it.' (3) So consider, may Allah have mercy on you, this great declaration concerning him, may peace be upon him, and the description of his city Mecca, and the declaration of what happened to him, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, with the Jews, the children of Israel – of His Almighty enabling him, may peace be upon him, to overpower them with devastating killing, captivity, and humiliation by imposing the jizya in all the lands of Islam.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage presents scriptural prophecies from the Old Testament (Isaiah and Ezekiel) as proofs of the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him). The author begins by quoting a prophecy from Isaiah: "ولا يخصم حتى توراته ينقاد الحق" (and he will not be argued down until his Torah leads to the truth). The author then exclaims over the greatness of this declaration concerning Muhammad, pointing out several aspects: (1) the phrase 'He will give commandments to the nations' implies a universal mission, which applies only to Muhammad; (2) the phrase 'Ahmad will praise' explicitly names the Prophet (Ahmad being another name of Muhammad); (3) the description of the 'thirsty wilderness' rejoicing refers to Mecca, which was devoid of prophets. The author then quotes another passage from Isaiah explicitly mentioning 'Ahmad' and the splendor of Lebanon (Syria) being given to the desert – interpreted as Mecca receiving the glory of Syria through Muhammad's mission. The author explains that 'thirsty' means lacking messengers, as most prophets were from Syria. Next, a quote from Isaiah declares that the one whom the ignorant Israelites call 'misled' is actually the owner of prophecy, refuting their denial. Finally, a passage from Ezekiel compares Israel to a vine that is uprooted and burned, after which a new plant is planted in the desert – symbolizing the rise of Islam in Mecca and the subsequent conquest and humiliation of the Jews. The author concludes by urging the reader to reflect on this clear testimony about Muhammad and his victory over the Israelites.

إشعياء
يوصي الأمم
أحمد
مكة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Old Testament prophecies about Muhammad are vague or allegorical.
Correction: The author insists these are explicit declarations, using phrases like 'تصريح عظيم' (great declaration) and pointing to specific names and descriptions.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the phrase 'Ahmad will praise' in the prophecy of Isaiah indicate?
A) A reference to a later Jewish king
B) An explicit mention of the name of Prophet Muhammad
C) A description of a future temple
D) A metaphorical expression for repentance

Key Takeaway
The first Isaiah prophecy contains three explicit indicators of Muhammad's prophethood: universal mission, his name, and his birthplace Mecca.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the Prophet's name 'Ahmad' is explicitly mentioned in Isaiah, do you feel a sense of awe at how Allah preserved this sign? Or does it leave you indifferent? What does your reaction reveal about your connection to the Prophet?
?
The prophecy says the thirsty wilderness (Mecca) will rejoice. Imagine you are a Meccan at the time of the Prophet's birth, unaware of this prophecy. How would you respond if someone told you that a prophet would arise from that barren land? Are you today also blind to the signs of Allah around you because they come from unexpected places?
?
The author marvels at the clarity of these indicators. Have you ever truly marvelled at the proofs of prophethood? Or do you take them for granted? What will you do this week to sincerely appreciate one sign of Muhammad's prophethood?

The Second Isaiah Prophecy: Ahmad and the Splendor of Mecca
Second Isaiah prophecy with interpretation about Mecca.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Isaiah's prophecy about a thirsty desert rejoicing through 'Ahmad' points to Mecca and the honor bestowed upon it.

Core Idea
Isaiah prophesies that Mecca, once devoid of prophets, will receive glory through 'Ahmad'.

This lesson focuses on a second prophecy from Isaiah that is even more explicit, directly naming 'Ahmad' and describing the transformation of a desert into a place of splendor. The author interprets this as referring to Mecca and the blessings brought by Prophet Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Read the prophecy and its interpretation
Read the passage from 'وفي صحف إشعياء' to the end of the second paragraph. Note the direct mention of 'Ahmad' and the description of the desert receiving the splendor of Lebanon.
2
Understand 'thirsty desert' as Mecca
The author explains that 'thirsty' means lacking prophets, and Mecca was indeed without prophets before Muhammad. The 'splendor of Lebanon' refers to the glory of Syria, which is given to Mecca through the Prophet.
This involves an allegorical interpretation of the prophecy.
3
Reflect on the honor of Mecca
Consider why the author emphasizes that Mecca was honored by being the birthplace of the most honorable prophet.

وفي صحفِ إشعياء عليه السلام : ( لتفرح أهل البادية العطشى ولتبتهج البراري والفلواتُ؛ لأنَّها ستعطى بأحمد محاسنَ لبنان وكمثل حسن الدساكير والرياض ((٢)
فانظر أيضاً إلى هذا التصريح الواضح باسمه عليه الصلاة والسلام، وبما أكرمَ اللهُ تعالى بهِ بلدَهُ مكَّةَ بسبب بركة وجوده ونشأته فيها، وبعثه منها، ومعنى كونها عطشى؛ أي : مِنَ الرُّسُلِ والأنبياء عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام؛ فإنَّ بلد معظمهم الشام، فأعطى اللهُ سبحانَهُ لمكة ببعث أشرف الخلق منها صلّى الله عليه وسلَّمَ محاسنَ لبنان؛ أي : الشامِ؛ لأنَّ لُبنانَ مِنْ جَبَالِهِ
وفي صُحُفِ إشعياء أيضاً عليهِ السلامُ : ( أَتَتْ أيام الافتقادِ، أَتَتْ أيامُ الكمال )، ثمَّ قال : ( لتعلموا يا بني إسرائيل الجاهلين : أنَّ الذي تُسَمُّونَهُ ضالاً هو صاحب النبوَّةِ، تَفتَرُونَ ذلكَ؛ على كثرة ذنوبكم وعظم فجوركم ((١)
وفي صُحُفِ حزقيال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام، يقولُ عن الله عزّ وجلَّ بعدما ذكر معاصي بني إسرائيل وشبههم بكَرْمةٍ؛ وهي شجرةُ العنب، قال : ( لم تلبث تلكَ الكَرْمَةُ أنْ قُلِعَتْ بالسَّخْطَةِ، ورُمِيَ بها على الأرض، وأحرقتِ السمائمُ ثمارها(٢) ، فعند ذلكَ غُرِسَ غرس في البدو، وفي الأرضِ المهملة العطشى، وخرجَتْ مِنْ أغصانها الفاضلة نار أكلَتْ تلكَ الكَرْمةَ، حتى لم يُوجَد فيها غُصْنُ قوي ولا قضيب ((٣) .
فاعتبر رحمَكَ اللهُ هذا التصريح العظيمَ بهِ عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ وبصفة بلدِهِ مكَّةَ، والتصريح بما وقع له صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ مَعَ اليهودِ بني إسرائيلَ مِنْ تمكينه تعالى له عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ منهم بالقتل الذريع والسبي والإذلالِ لهم بضرب الجزية في جميع بلاد الإسلام .
And he will not be argued down until his Torah leads to the truth. (1) So consider, may Allah have mercy on you, this great declaration concerning our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, from multiple aspects: such as his saying, 'He will give commandments to the nations' – for that necessitates his being sent to all of them, and that has not been established except for our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace; and his saying, 'Ahmad will praise' – this is an explicit mention of his name; and his saying, 'The thirsty wilderness will rejoice, and its inhabitants...' to the end – for it is not hidden that these are descriptions of Mecca. And in the scriptures of Isaiah, peace be upon him: 'Let the thirsty desert dwellers rejoice, and let the barren lands and wildernesses be glad; for they will be given by Ahmad the splendors of Lebanon and like the beauty of villages and meadows.' (2) So look also at this clear declaration of his name, may peace and blessings be upon him, and of what Allah Almighty honored his city Mecca with, due to the blessing of his existence and upbringing therein, and his being sent from it. And the meaning of its being 'thirsty' – i.e., devoid of messengers and prophets, may peace and blessings be upon them; for the land of most of them is Syria. So Allah, glorified be He, gave to Mecca, by sending the most honorable of creation from it, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, the splendors of Lebanon – i.e., Syria; because Lebanon is among its mountains. And in the scriptures of Isaiah also, peace be upon him: 'The days of visitation have come, the days of perfection have come,' then he said: 'Let you know, O ignorant children of Israel, that the one you call a misled person is the owner of prophecy; you falsely accuse him, because of your many sins and great immorality.' (1) And in the scriptures of Ezekiel the prophet, may peace and blessings be upon him, he says about Allah, mighty and majestic, after mentioning the sins of the children of Israel and comparing them to a vine – which is the grapevine – he said: 'That vine did not last; it was pulled up in wrath, and thrown to the ground, and the hot winds burned its fruits. (2) Then at that time, a plant was planted in the desert, in the neglected thirsty land, and from its abundant branches a fire came out and devoured that vine, until no strong branch or rod was found in it.' (3) So consider, may Allah have mercy on you, this great declaration concerning him, may peace be upon him, and the description of his city Mecca, and the declaration of what happened to him, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, with the Jews, the children of Israel – of His Almighty enabling him, may peace be upon him, to overpower them with devastating killing, captivity, and humiliation by imposing the jizya in all the lands of Islam.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage presents scriptural prophecies from the Old Testament (Isaiah and Ezekiel) as proofs of the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him). The author begins by quoting a prophecy from Isaiah: "ولا يخصم حتى توراته ينقاد الحق" (and he will not be argued down until his Torah leads to the truth). The author then exclaims over the greatness of this declaration concerning Muhammad, pointing out several aspects: (1) the phrase 'He will give commandments to the nations' implies a universal mission, which applies only to Muhammad; (2) the phrase 'Ahmad will praise' explicitly names the Prophet (Ahmad being another name of Muhammad); (3) the description of the 'thirsty wilderness' rejoicing refers to Mecca, which was devoid of prophets. The author then quotes another passage from Isaiah explicitly mentioning 'Ahmad' and the splendor of Lebanon (Syria) being given to the desert – interpreted as Mecca receiving the glory of Syria through Muhammad's mission. The author explains that 'thirsty' means lacking messengers, as most prophets were from Syria. Next, a quote from Isaiah declares that the one whom the ignorant Israelites call 'misled' is actually the owner of prophecy, refuting their denial. Finally, a passage from Ezekiel compares Israel to a vine that is uprooted and burned, after which a new plant is planted in the desert – symbolizing the rise of Islam in Mecca and the subsequent conquest and humiliation of the Jews. The author concludes by urging the reader to reflect on this clear testimony about Muhammad and his victory over the Israelites.

أحمد
مكة
لبنان
الشام

Checkpoint
Why does the author interpret 'thirsty desert' in Isaiah's prophecy as referring to Mecca?
A) Because Mecca had abundant water
B) Because Mecca was devoid of prophets before Muhammad
C) Because Mecca is a desert city
D) Because the prophecy mentions 'Ahmad'

Key Takeaway
Isaiah explicitly prophesies that through 'Ahmad', the barren desert (Mecca) will receive the splendor of the prophetic land (Syria).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The desert dwellers were commanded to rejoice because of the gift of Ahmad. Do you truly rejoice in the Prophet’s coming? What would change in your daily life if you lived with that joy as a constant reality?
?
Your own heart may feel like a ‘thirsty desert’—barren of guidance or spiritual life. What specific area of your life needs the ‘splendors of Lebanon’ (prophetic wisdom) that only the Prophet can bring? What is one step you will take this week to invite his example into that area?
?
Mecca received its honor through the Prophet’s presence and upbringing. How can your home, family, or community become a place where the Prophet’s character is present and honored? What is one habit you can start or stop to make that happen?

The Ezekiel Prophecy: The Vine, the Desert, and Victory over the Jews
Third Isaiah prophecy and Ezekiel prophecy with conclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how prophecies from Isaiah and Ezekiel foretell the rejection of the Prophet by the Israelites and the subsequent triumph of Islam.

Core Idea
Old Testament prophecies depict the Israelites' rejection of the true prophet and the rise of Islam in their place.

The final section presents two more prophecies: one from Isaiah that rebukes the Israelites for calling the Prophet 'misled', and another from Ezekiel that allegorically describes the replacement of the people of Israel with a new community from the desert. The author concludes by reflecting on the historical fulfillment of these prophecies.

Guided Path
1
Read the Isaiah rebuke
Read the passage from 'وفي صحف إشعياء أيضاً' up to 'عظم فجوركم'. Note how the prophecy addresses the 'ignorant children of Israel' and declares that the one they call 'misled' is actually the owner of prophecy.
2
Read the Ezekiel allegory
Read the Ezekiel passage from 'وفي صحف حزقيال' to 'قضيب'. Understand the allegory of the vine (Israel) being uprooted and a new plant growing in the desert.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The author draws a parallel to the historical conflict between Muslims and Jews, and the victory of Islam over the Jewish tribes.

?

?

?

Do you live each day with the urgency that you are part of the greatest victory in history, or have you become complacent and disconnected from the mission of your Prophet?

Prophecy from Isaiah about the Coming Prophet
The author cites a prophecy from Isaiah about the coming prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a biblical prophecy from Isaiah is used as evidence for the prophethood of Muhammad.

Core Idea
Isaiah's prophecy explicitly identifies the rejected prophet as the true possessor of prophethood.

This lesson presents a scriptural proof from the Book of Isaiah. The author cites a prophetic statement that announces the arrival of 'the days of visitation and perfection' and rebukes the Israelites for falsely labeling the true prophet as misguided. Let's examine how this passage serves as evidence for Muhammad's prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
First, read the Arabic source passage and the literal English translation. Notice the direct tone of the prophecy.
2
Understand the context
The author is citing Isaiah, a recognized prophet in Judaism and Christianity, to show that earlier scriptures foretold Muhammad's coming. The 'days of visitation and perfection' refer to the time of his prophethood.
3
Identify the key claim
Isaiah says that the one the Israelites call 'misguided' is actually the possessor of prophethood. This directly counters the Jewish rejection of Muhammad.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why the author uses this proof: to demonstrate that the coming of Muhammad was predicted in earlier scriptures and that his rejection was unjust.

وفي صُحُفِ إشعياء أيضاً عليهِ السلامُ : ( أَتَتْ أيام الافتقادِ ، أَتَتْ أيامُ الكمال ) ، ثمَّ قال : ( لتعلموا يا بني إسرائيل الجاهلين : : أنَّ الذي تُسَمُّونَهُ ضالاً هو صاحب النبوَّةِ ، تَفتَرُونَ ذلكَ ؛ على كثرة ذنوبكم وعظم فجوركم ((١)

Then he said: 'Know, O ignorant children of Israel, that the one you call a misguided person is the possessor of prophethood; you fabricate that because of the abundance of your sins and the greatness of your wickedness.' (1)
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is a scriptural citation from the Book of Isaiah. The author presents Isaiah's prophecy as clear proof of Muhammad's prophethood. The prophecy states that 'the days of visitation and perfection' have arrived, referring to the coming of a prophet. Then it rebukes the Israelites for falsely calling that prophet 'misguided' when he is in fact the true prophet. The author uses this to show that the Jewish scriptures themselves testified to Muhammad's coming and that the Jews rejected him unjustly.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The prophecy states that the Israelites' false accusation stems from 'the abundance of your sins and the greatness of your wickedness'. ?
The 'days of perfection' have come with the final prophet. Are you truly living as if you believe that this message is the ultimate truth? What concrete change will you make this week to align your life with the perfection of that prophethood, rather than following your own whims?

Ezekiel's Prophecy of the Vine and the Rise of Islam
The author cites Ezekiel's prophecy of the vine uprooted and replanted in the wilderness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a biblical prophecy about a vine is interpreted by the author as a clear prediction of Prophet Muhammad's mission and the rise of Islam.

Core Idea
Ezekiel's vine prophecy foretells the rise of Islam from the desert.

In this lesson, we read a citation from the prophet Ezekiel that describes the destruction of a vine representing the Children of Israel, followed by a new planting in the wilderness. The author then connects this directly to Prophet Muhammad and his companions, showing how the prophecy points to the emergence of Islam in Mecca and the eventual triumph over the Jews. Let's examine the text carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the full Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the prophecy structure: a vine uprooted, a new planting in the desert, and a fire that destroys the original vine.
The passage includes a citation from Ezekiel and the author's interpretive commentary.
2
Identify the prophecy's components
The vine represents the Children of Israel. It is uprooted with wrath, its fruits burnt. Then a new planting appears in the desert (a barren land). Finally, fire from its branches consumes the original vine.
The desert planting is key—it symbolizes a new community emerging from an unlikely place.
3
Understand the author's application
The author explicitly states that the new planting refers to Prophet Muhammad and his city Mecca. The fire from the branches represents the Muslims' victories over the Jews, including killing, captivity, and jizya.
This is a direct claim that the prophecy foretells Muhammad's mission and the spread of Islam.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why the author considers this a 'great clear statement'. It serves as a proof from earlier scriptures for the prophethood of Muhammad and the truth of Islam.
This lesson shows how Muslim scholars used biblical prophecies as evidence.

وفي صُحُفِ حزقيال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام ، يقولُ عن الله عزّ وجلَّ بعدما ذكر معاصي بني إسرائيل وشبههم بكَرْمةٍ ؛ وهي شجرةُ العنب ، قال : ( لم تلبث تلكَ الكَرْمَةُ أنْ قُلِعَتْ بالسَّخْطَةِ ، ورُمِيَ بها على الأرض ، وأحرقتِ السمائمُ ثمارها(٢) ، فعند ذلكَ غُرِسَ غرس في البدو ، وفي الأرضِ المهملة العطشى ، وخرجَتْ مِنْ أغصانها الفاضلة نار أكلَتْ تلكَ الكَرْمةَ ، حتى لم يُوجَد فيها غُصْنُ قوي ولا قضيب ((٣) . فاعتبر رحمَكَ اللهُ هذا التصريح العظيمَ بهِ عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ وبصفة بلدِهِ مَكَّةَ ، والتصريح بما وقع له صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ مَعَ اليهودِ بني إسرائيلَ مِنْ تمكينه تعالى له عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ منهم بالقتل الذريع والسبي والإذلالِ لهم بضرب الجزية في جميع بلاد الإسلام .
And in the scriptures of Ezekiel the prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, he says about God Almighty after mentioning the sins of the Children of Israel and likening them to a vine, which is the grape tree: 'That vine did not last long before it was uprooted with wrath, thrown onto the ground, and the hot winds burnt its fruits. Then a planting was planted in the desert, in the neglected and thirsty land, and from its excellent branches came out fire that consumed that vine, until no strong branch or twig was found in it.' So take heed, may God have mercy on you, of this great clear statement about him, peace and blessings be upon him, and about the description of his city Mecca, and the clear statement about what happened to him, may God bless him and grant him peace, with the Jews of the Children of Israel from His Almighty enabling him, peace be upon him, against them by severe killing, captivity, and humiliation by imposing jizya in all lands of Islam.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is a scriptural citation from Ezekiel followed by the author's commentary. First, the author presents Ezekiel's allegory of the vine representing Israel. The vine is uprooted and destroyed because of disobedience, then a new planting appears in the wilderness—a reference to the emergence of a new community. The author then directly applies this to Prophet Muhammad: the 'new planting' refers to Muhammad's mission in Mecca (a desert land), and the fire from its branches represents his victories over the Jews. The author emphasizes that this prophecy explicitly mentions Mecca and the conquests of Islam. The lesson concludes with an exhortation to reflect on this clear prophecy.

Correction: The author shows that the prophecy clearly predicts the coming of Prophet Muhammad and the rise of Islam, based on the 'new planting' in the desert and the fire that consumes the original vine.

Daniel's Prophecy of the Stone and Muhammad's Eternal Kingdom
The author interprets Daniel's dream as a prophecy of Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author interprets Daniel's dream of the stone as a clear prophecy foretelling Muhammad's prophethood and eternal kingdom.

Core Idea
Biblical prophecy points to Muhammad as the final prophet.

This lesson presents a detailed narrative from Daniel's prophecy, where the dream of a statue and a stone is interpreted as foretelling the rise of a divine kingdom. The author then explicitly applies this to our Prophet Muhammad, emphasizing that his prophethood and the kingdom of his community are eternal and unmatched. Let us examine the passage and its interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Dream Account
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand Nebuchadnezzar's dream of the statue and the stone that destroys it.
Notice the detail in describing the statue's materials and the stone's action.
2
Identify the Interpretation
Identify what each part of the statue represents according to Daniel: different empires and kingdoms.
The stone is interpreted as a new divine kingdom.
3
Apply to Muhammad
Understand how the author applies the stone to Muhammad: the religion of a prophet and an eternal kingdom at the end of time.
The author stresses that Muhammad's prophethood is everlasting.
4
Reflect on the Claim
Consider why the author presents this as a clear proof of Muhammad's prophethood and how it refutes those who deny biblical references to him.

وقالَ دانيال النبيُّ عليهِ السلامُ وقد سألَهُ الملكُ بُخْتَنَصَّرُ عن منامة رآها ، وطلبَهُ أنْ يخبره بها وبتفسيرها ، فقال له دانیال عليه السلام : أيُّها الملكُ ؛ رأيت صنماً بارع الجمالِ ؛ أعلاهُ مِنْ ذهبٍ ، ووسطهُ مِنْ فضَّةٍ ، وأسفلُهُ مِنْ نحاس ، وساقاهُ مِنْ حديد ، ورجلاهُ مِنْ فَخَارٍ فبينَما أَنتَ تنظرُ إليه قد أعجبَكَ إِذْ نزلَ حجرٌ مِنَ السَّماءِ فكسرَهُ ، وضربَ رأسَ الصنمِ فطحنه ، حتى اختلط ذهبُهُ وفَضَّتُهُ ونحاسُهُ وحديدُهُ وفَخَارُهُ ، ثمَّ إِنَّ الحجر ربا وعَظُمَ حتى ملأ الأرضَ كلَّها فقالَ لَهُ بُخْتَنَصَّرُ : صدقت ، فأخبرني بتأويلها ، فقالَ دانيال عليهِ السلامُ : أَمَّا الصنمُ فأممٌ مختلفة في أوَّلِ الزمان وفي وسطه وفي آخرِه ؛ فالرأسُ مِنَ الذهب أنتَ أيُّها الملكُ ، والفضة ابنك بعدَكَ والنحاس الرومُ ، والحديد الفرسُ ، والفَخَارُ أُمَّتانِ ضعيفتانِ تملكهما امرأتان باليمن والشام ، والحجرُ النازلُ مِنَ السماء دينُ نبيٌّ ومُلْكُ أبدي يكونُ في آخرِ الزمانِ ، يغلبُ الأمم كلَّها ، ثم يعظم حتى يملاً الأرض كلَّها كما ملأها هذا الحجر (۱) فانظر هذا التصريحَ الجليَّ المطابق لسيّدِنا ومولانا ونبينا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ؛ فإِنَّهُ الذي بُعِثَ في آخر الزمانِ ، وهو الذي نبوتُهُ ومُلْكُ أُمَّتِهِ أبدي إلى قيام الساعةِ ؛ إذ لا نبيَّ بعدَهُ صَلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، ولا نسخ لشرعِهِ الشريف ما بقيَتِ الدنيا ، وهو الذي بُعِثَ إلى
And Daniel the prophet, peace be upon him, said when King Nebuchadnezzar asked him about a dream he saw and asked him to tell him about it and its interpretation. Daniel said to him: 'O king, you saw a statue of surpassing beauty; its head was of gold, its middle of silver, its lower part of brass, its legs of iron, and its feet of clay. While you were looking at it and admiring it, a stone came down from heaven and broke it, struck the head of the statue and crushed it, until its gold, silver, brass, iron, and clay were mixed together. Then the stone grew and became great until it filled all the earth.' Nebuchadnezzar said: 'You have spoken truth, so tell me its interpretation.' Daniel said: 'As for the statue, it represents different nations in the beginning, middle, and end of time: the head of gold is you, O king; the silver is your son after you; the brass is the Romans; the iron is the Persians; and the clay is two weak nations ruled by two women in Yemen and Syria. The stone that came down from heaven is the religion of a prophet and an eternal kingdom that will come at the end of time; it will overcome all nations, then become great until it fills all the earth as this stone filled it.' (1) So look at this clear statement matching our master, our lord, and our prophet Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, for he is the one sent at the end of time, and his prophethood and the kingdom of his nation are eternal until the Day of Resurrection, for there is no prophet after him, may God bless him and grant him peace, and no abrogation of his noble law as long as the world remains, and he is the one sent to...
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed account of Daniel's interpretation of Nebuchadnezzar's dream. The dream is a four-part statue representing successive empires: Babylonian, Median, Persian, Greek (or Roman), and then weak divided kingdoms. The stone that destroys the statue represents a divine kingdom that will crush all others and fill the earth. The author applies this to Muhammad: the stone is the religion (dīn) of a prophet—Muhammad—and his eternal kingdom. The author emphasizes that Muhammad was sent at the end of time, his prophethood and the rule of his community are everlasting until the Day of Judgment, and his law is not abrogated. The passage ends mid-sentence but the main argument is complete.

Correction: The author asserts that the stone represents a prophet and eternal kingdom at the end of time, which he argues matches Muhammad perfectly as the final prophet.

Daniel's Prophecy of the Dream as Proof for Muhammad
Sanusi recounts Daniel's interpretation of Nebuchadnezzar's dream as a prophecy fulfilled by Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a prophecy from the book of Daniel is used as evidence for the prophethood of Muhammad (SAW) in classical Islamic theology.

Core Idea
Ancient scriptures point to Muhammad through clear prophecies.

This passage presents a remarkable prophecy from the book of Daniel, where the interpretation of Nebuchadnezzar's dream is seen as a direct prediction of the coming of Islam and the final prophet. Sanusi uses this as a powerful proof from earlier scriptures. Let's read the original account and see how it aligns with the mission of Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Read the dream narrative
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Notice the details of the idol and the stone that descends from heaven.
2
Understand the interpretation
Daniel interprets each metal as a different kingdom. Identify what each part represents: head of gold, silver, brass, iron, and clay.
The head of gold is Nebuchadnezzar himself.
3
Identify the stone's meaning
The stone is explained as the religion of a prophet and an eternal kingdom at the end of time. Note its growth to fill the earth.
4
See the application to Muhammad
Sanusi explicitly links this stone to Muhammad (SAW). Observe how he describes Muhammad's eternal prophethood, universal mission, and the unity of his community.
This is the central claim of the passage.
5
Reflect on the broader evidence
Consider the concluding statement that previous scriptures are full of such clear prophecies about Muhammad. How does this strengthen the proof?
This reinforces the argument from earlier revelations.
