⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالَ دانيال النبيُّ عليهِ السلامُ وقد سألَهُ الملكُ بُخْتَنَصَّرُ عن منامة رآها ، وطلبَهُ أنْ يخبره بها وبتفسيرها ، فقال له دانیال عليه السلام : أيُّها الملكُ ؛ رأيت صنماً بارع الجمالِ ؛ أعلاهُ مِنْ ذهبٍ ، ووسطهُ مِنْ فضَّةٍ ، وأسفلُهُ مِنْ نحاس ، وساقاهُ مِنْ حديد ، ورجلاهُ مِنْ فَخَارٍ فبينَما أَنتَ تنظرُ إليه قد أعجبَكَ إِذْ نزلَ حجرٌ مِنَ السَّماءِ فكسرَهُ ، وضربَ رأسَ الصنمِ فطحنه ، حتى اختلط ذهبُهُ وفَضَّتُهُ ونحاسُهُ وحديدُهُ وفَخَارُهُ ، ثمَّ إِنَّ الحجر ربا وعَظُمَ حتى ملأ الأرضَ كلَّها فقالَ لَهُ بُخْتَنَصَّرُ : صدقت ، فأخبرني بتأويلها ، فقالَ دانيال عليهِ السلامُ : أَمَّا الصنمُ فأممٌ مختلفة في أوَّلِ الزمان وفي وسطه وفي آخرِه ؛ فالرأسُ مِنَ الذهب أنتَ أيُّها الملكُ ، والفضة ابنك بعدَكَ والنحاس الرومُ ، والحديد الفرسُ ، والفَخَارُ أُمَّتانِ ضعيفتانِ تملكهما امرأتان باليمن والشام ، والحجرُ النازلُ مِنَ السماء دينُ نبيٍّ ومُلْكُ أبدي يكونُ في آخرِ الزمانِ ، يغلبُ الأمم كلَّها ، ثم يعظم حتى يملاً الأرض كلَّها كما ملأها هذا الحجر (۱) فانظر هذا التصريحَ الجليَّ المطابق لسيّدِنا ومولانا ونبينا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ؛ فإِنَّهُ الذي بُعِثَ في آخر الزمانِ ، وهو الذي نبوتُهُ ومُلْكُ أُمَّتِهِ أبدي إلى قيام الساعةِ ؛ إذ لا نبيَّ بعدَهُ صَلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، ولا نسخ لشرعِهِ الشريف ما بقيَتِ الدنيا ، وهو الذي بُعِثَ إلى جميع الأمم ، وظهر عليها كلّها ، وخلط بين أجناسها ، وجعلها على اختلافِ أديانها واختلافِ لغاتِها جنساً واحداً ، وعلى لغة واحدة ؛ إذ كلُّهم يقرؤون القرآن بلغة العرب ، وبها يُصلُّونَ... إلى غير ذلكَ ، وكلُّهم يدينون بدين واحدٍ ؛ وهو دين الإسلام . وبالجملة : فنصوص الكتب السابقة على ثبوتِ نبوَّةِ سيّدِنا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ وتعظيم شأنِهِ ، وإيصاءات الأنبياء الماضينَ عليهِ ، وإشادتهم ذكرَهُ ، وتبشيراتُ الأحبار به .. لا تكاد تنحصر وثبوت رسالتِهِ وشرفه على كلّ ما خلق مولانا تبارك وتعالى . . أجلى مِنَ الشمس
And Daniel the Prophet, peace be upon him, said when King Nebuchadnezzar asked him about a dream he had seen, and requested that he inform him of it and its interpretation: Daniel, peace be upon him, said to him: O king, you saw an idol of exquisite beauty; its top of gold, its middle of silver, its lower part of brass, its legs of iron, and its feet of clay. While you were looking at it, admiring it, a stone descended from the sky and broke it, and struck the head of the idol and crushed it until its gold, silver, brass, iron, and clay were mixed together. Then the stone grew and became great until it filled all the earth. Nebuchadnezzar said to him: You have spoken truth; so tell me its interpretation. Daniel, peace be upon him, said: As for the idol, it is different nations in the beginning of time, in its middle, and in its end. The head of gold is you, O king; the silver is your son after you; the brass is the Romans; the iron is the Persians; the clay is two weak nations ruled by two women in Yemen and Syria. And the stone descending from the sky is the religion of a prophet and an eternal kingdom that will be at the end of time; it will overcome all nations, then it will grow until it fills all the earth as this stone filled it. (1) So look at this clear statement matching our Master, our Patron, and our Prophet Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace. For he is the one sent at the end of time, and his prophethood and the kingdom of his community are eternal until the Day of Resurrection, since there is no prophet after him, may God bless him and grant him peace, nor abrogation of his noble law as long as the world remains. And he is the one sent to all nations, and he prevailed over all of them, and mixed their races, and made them, despite the difference of their religions and languages, one race and one language, since all of them recite the Quran in the language of the Arabs, and with it they pray... and so on; and all of them adhere to one religion, which is the religion of Islam. In summary: the texts of the previous scriptures concerning the confirmation of the prophethood of our Master and Patron Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, and the exaltation of his rank, and the injunctions of the past prophets concerning him, and their praise of his mention, and the glad tidings of the rabbis about him... are nearly uncountable, and the confirmation of his message and his honor over all that our Lord, Blessed and Exalted, created... is clearer than the sun.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a proof from previous scriptures for the prophethood of Muhammad (SAW). The author recounts the story of Daniel's interpretation of Nebuchadnezzar's dream. In the dream, an idol with different metals (gold, silver, brass, iron, clay) is struck by a stone that breaks it and grows to fill the earth. Daniel interprets the metals as successive kingdoms: Nebuchadnezzar himself, his son, the Romans, the Persians, and two weak nations. The stone represents the religion of a prophet and an eternal kingdom at the end of time. The author then explicitly applies this to Muhammad: he is the prophet sent at the end of time, his prophethood and community are eternal until the Last Day, with no prophet after him and no abrogation of his law. He was sent to all nations, united them in faith and language (Arabic for worship). The concluding paragraph emphasizes that the previous scriptures are full of such clear prophecies about Muhammad, his prophethood, and his honor, being clearer than the sun. The passage thus uses a specific biblical prophecy as a factual (and divinely revealed) sign of Muhammad's truth, arguing that the details match perfectly.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This proof is weak because it relies on biblical texts that Muslims do not consider preserved.
Correction: Sanusi treats the prophecy as a preserved revelation from God confirming Islam, and Muslims accept that earlier scriptures contained true prophecies that have been fulfilled.

?
This prophecy was given centuries before Muhammad (SAW) was born, showing that Allah has planned the final victory of Islam. When you look at the weakness and division among Muslims today, do you still believe that this kingdom is eternal? How does that belief change your hope and your actions? What are you doing to actively belong to that eternal kingdom?

The Consensus on the Prophet's Superiority over Creation
Sanusi declares the consensus on the Prophet's superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet Muhammad's superiority over all creation is an established consensus (ijma') supported by countless Quranic and Sunnah evidences, and that any innovation contrary to this is dismissed.

Core Idea
The Prophet's superiority is a matter of consensus, not opinion.

Sanusi begins by asserting a foundational Sunni belief: the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) is superior to all creation. This is not merely a personal view but an agreed-upon doctrine (ijma') with abundant scriptural evidence. The author also warns against those who innovate contrary beliefs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the strong language about consensus and the dismissal of innovators.
The passage uses the phrase 'لا يُلتفت' which shows rejection.
2
Identify the claim
What exactly does Sanusi claim is established? It is the consensus on the Prophet's superiority.
This is a doctrinal claim based on ijma'.
3
Consider the significance
Why does Sanusi mention that the evidences are uncountable? To emphasize the strength of the proof.
This counters any attempt to deny the superiority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ انعقاد الإجماع على أفضليته عليه الصلاة والسلام ]
وقد ثبت الإجماع على أفضليَّتِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ على الخلقِ ، وشواهد ذلكَ مِنَ الكتاب والسنَّةِ لا تكاد تنحصر ، ولا يُلتفتُ إلى مَنِ ابتدع وحاولَ غير ذلكَ (۱)
ويكفيكَ في معرفة شرفِهِ وعُلُوّ منزلتِهِ عندَ اللهِ تعالى على المخلوقاتِ عموماً بلا استثناء .. ما أُجْمَعَ عليهِ مِنَ التقدُّم للشفاعةِ الكبرى في موطن الآخرةِ ، وتنويهِ اللهِ تعالى هناكَ بِقَدْرِهِ والرَّفْعِ لمنزلتِهِ والإكرام له ؛ حيث اجتمع الأوَّلون والآخرون وجميع الأنبياء (۱) في هامش ( و ) : ( أشار إلى الزمخشري في أماكن من ( تفسيره » عفا الله عنه ) .
[ The establishment of consensus on his superiority, peace and blessings be upon him ]
And the consensus on his superiority, may God bless him and grant him peace, over creation has been established, and its evidences from the Book and the Sunnah are nearly uncountable, and no attention is paid to whoever innovated and attempted otherwise. (1)
And it suffices you in knowing his honor and the highness of his rank with God Almighty over all creatures generally without exception... what has been agreed upon concerning his precedence for the Great Intercession in the abode of the Hereafter, and God's exaltation there of his worth, and the raising of his rank, and the honoring of him, when the first and the last and all the prophets gather. (1) Marginal note (و): (He referred to al-Zamakhshari in places of his Tafsir; may God forgive him).
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a declaration of the consensus (ijma') on the superiority of the Prophet Muhammad over all creation. The author begins by stating that the consensus on his superiority is firmly established, and the evidences from the Quran and Sunnah are innumerable. He dismisses any innovator who attempts to deny this, saying no attention should be paid to them. Then he presents a key proof: the agreed-upon fact that the Prophet will have precedence in the Great Intercession (ash-shafa'ah al-kubra) on the Day of Judgment. This event, where all previous and later generations and all prophets gather, shows God's exaltation of the Prophet's rank and honor. The marginal note indicates a reference to al-Zamakhshari's Tafsir as a source for some of these points. The passage thus conveys a core Sunni belief: the Prophet's superiority is not merely a personal opinion but a matter of consensus supported by clear textual evidence.

Key Terms
إجماع
أفضلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's superiority is based on personal opinion or affection.
Correction: Sanusi establishes it as a matter of consensus (ijma') with overwhelming scriptural support.

Checkpoint

A) They are few but clear

D) They are only from the Sunnah

Key Takeaway
The Prophet Muhammad's superiority over creation is an established consensus (ijma') supported by countless scriptural proofs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage states that those who innovate contrary to this consensus are to be ignored. Is there any doubt in your mind about this teaching that you need to actively dismiss for the sake of following the mainstream of Ahl al-Sunnah?
?
With the evidences being 'nearly uncountable,' how many have you sincerely pondered? Will you commit today to studying at least one verse or hadith that proves his superiority, and let it reshape your reverence for him?

The Great Intercession as Proof of the Prophet's Superiority
Sanusi presents the Great Intercession as proof of the Prophet's superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will see how the Prophet's role in the Great Intercession (ash-shafa'ah al-kubra) on Judgment Day serves as a key proof of his supreme rank.

Core Idea
The Great Intercession proves the Prophet's highest status.

After stating the consensus, Sanusi presents a powerful piece of evidence: the agreed-upon fact that the Prophet will intercede first on the Day of Judgment. This event, where all creation and all prophets gather, demonstrates God's exaltation of the Prophet's rank above all others.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Focus on the phrase 'ما أُجْمَعَ عليهِ مِنَ التقدُّم للشفاعةِ الكبرى' and the description of God's exaltation.
The word 'يكفيك' indicates this is sufficient proof.
2
Understand the event
The Great Intercession is a specific event where the Prophet will be given precedence to intercede for all mankind. This shows his high rank.
All prophets and people will be present, yet he is the first.
3
Reflect on the implications
This event is not just a story; it is a doctrinal proof recognized by consensus. It shows God's special honor for the Prophet.

The Consensus and the Great Intercession: Proofs of the Prophet's Supreme Rank
Sanusi combines consensus and the intercession narrative to argue for the Prophet's absolute superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the consensus of the Muslim community and the narrative of the Great Intercession definitively establish the Prophet Muhammad's superiority over all creation.

Core Idea
Consensus and the Great Intercession together prove the Prophet's unmatched honor.

In this passage, Sanusi presents two intertwined arguments for the Prophet's supreme rank: the unanimous consensus of the community (ijma') and the dramatic event of the Great Intercession on the Day of Judgment. He calls upon the reader to reflect on God's special address to the Prophet in that terrifying scene as the clearest proof of his status. This lesson unpacks both the logical force of consensus and the theological weight of the intercession narrative.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping, then read the translation. Note how the author moves from general claims to a specific, vivid narrative.
The opening lines may seem unrelated but set the stage for the Prophet's universal significance.
2
Identify the consensus claim
Find the sentence where Sanusi states that consensus (ijma') has been established on the Prophet's superiority. Note that he dismisses any dissent as innovation.
Consensus is a major source of authority in Islamic theology.
3
Examine the intercession narrative
Read the description of the Day of Judgment carefully. Notice who is afraid, who is not, and what the Prophet says and does.
The Prophet's confidence is highlighted: he says 'I am for it' without hesitation.
4
Reflect on God's address
Pay attention to the words God speaks to the Prophet: 'Raise your head... ask, you will be given; intercede, you will be granted intercession.' Ponder what this reveals about the Prophet's rank.
This direct and honorific address is unprecedented on that day.
5
Understand the conclusion
The author ends by asserting that no one is more honored by God than Muhammad. Connect this back to consensus and the intercession story as proof.

جميع الأمم، وظهر عليها كلّها، وخلط بين أجناسها، وجعلها على اختلافِ أديانها واختلافِ لغاتِها جنساً واحداً، وعلى لغة واحدة؛ إذ كلُّهم يقرؤون القرآن بلغة العرب، وبها يُصلُّونَ... إلى غير ذلكَ، وكلُّهم يدينون بدين واحدٍ؛ وهو دين الإسلام. وبالجملة: فنصوص الكتب السابقة على ثبوتِ نبوَّةِ سيّدِنا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ وتعظيم شأنِهِ، وإيصاءات الأنبياء الماضينَ عليهِ، وإشادتهم ذكرَهُ، وتبشيراتُ الأحبار به .. لا تكاد تنحصر وثبوت رسالتِهِ وشرفه على كلّ ما خلق مولانا تبارك وتعالى.. أجلى مِنَ الشمس. [انعقاد الإجماع على أفضليته عليه الصلاة والسلام] وقد ثبت الإجماع على أفضليَّتِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ على الخلقِ، وشواهد ذلكَ مِنَ الكتاب والسنَّةِ لا تكاد تنحصر، ولا يُلتفتُ إلى مَنِ ابتدع وحاولَ غير ذلكَ. ويكفيكَ في معرفة شرفِهِ وعُلُوّ منزلتِهِ عندَ اللهِ تعالى على المخلوقاتِ عموماً بلا استثناء .. ما أُجْمَعَ عليهِ مِنَ التقدُّم للشفاعةِ الكبرى في موطن الآخرةِ، وتنويهِ اللهِ تعالى هناكَ بِقَدْرِهِ والرَّفْعِ لمنزلتِهِ والإكرام له؛ حيث اجتمع الأوَّلون والآخرون وجميع الأنبياء والمرسلين والملائكة كلهم والمقرَّبينَ، وعم الخطب واشتدَّ الهول وكلٌّ مشغول بنفسِهِ، خائفٌ هائبٌ لجلالِ المولى العظيم، جاثِ على ركبتيه؛ لما يرى في ذلك اليومِ مِنَ الخطر والهول الجسيم، ولا يتجاسر أحدٌ في ذلك اليوم الهائل على مخاطبة المولى تبارك وتعالى في رفعِ شيء ممَّا نزلَ .. سوى عبدِهِ وخاتم رُسُلِهِ، وعروس مملكته وسرها وإكسيرها، وسيّدِ كلَّ ما خَلَقَ مولانا جل وعلا، صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ، فيقولُ عند ما ينتهي الناسُ إليهِ في طلب الشفاعة إلى المولى تبارك وتعالى: «أَنَا لَهَا»، لا يخافُ ولا يُهِمُّهُ أمر نفسِهِ، ولا يتتعتع، ويذهب حتى يسجد تحت العرش، فيقول المولى جلَّ وعلا: (أَرْفَعْ رَأْسَكَ يَا مُحَمَّدُ، وَقُلْ يُسْمَعْ لَكَ، وَسَلْ تُعْطَهْ وَاشْفَعْ تُشَفْعْ). فانظُرْ رحمَكَ اللهُ هذا الخطاب العزيز اللطيف الشريف لهُ عليهِ الصلاة والسلامُ مِنْ مولانا تبارك وتعالى في ذلك اليوم الهائل، الذي غضبَ فيه سبحانَهُ غضباً لم يغضب قبلَهُ مثلَهُ، ولا يغضب بعده مثلَهُ كيف وهو صريح بالمعنى بلا نزاع ولا ريب ولا احتمالٍ أَنَّهُ لا أكرمَ من نبينا وسيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ على اللهِ تبارك وتعالى؟! وفي الحديثِ: (أنَّه صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أَوَّلُ مَنْ يَفْرَعُ بَابَ الْجَنَّةِ، فَيَقُولُ رِضْوَانُ خَازِنُهَا عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ: مَنْ ؟ فَيَقُولُ: مُحَمَّدٌ
All nations, and it appeared upon all of them, and mixed among their races, and made them, despite the difference of their religions and the difference of their languages, one race, and upon one language; since all of them recite the Qur'an in the language of the Arabs, and with it they pray... and so on, and all of them follow one religion; and it is the religion of Islam. In summary: the texts of the previous books regarding the establishment of the prophethood of our master and our lord Muhammad (peace and blessings be upon him) and the magnification of his status, and the bequests of the past prophets concerning him, and their praise of his mention, and the announcements of the rabbis about him... are almost limitless, and the establishment of his message and his honor over all that our lord, Blessed and Most High, created... is clearer than the sun. [The establishment of consensus on his superiority – peace and blessings be upon him] And consensus has been established on his superiority (peace and blessings be upon him) over creation, and the evidences of that from the Book and the Sunnah are almost limitless, and no attention is paid to whoever innovated and attempted otherwise. And it suffices you in knowing his honor and the highness of his station with God Most High over all creatures in general without exception... what has been unanimously agreed upon regarding his precedence for the great intercession in the abode of the Hereafter, and God Most High's declaration there of his worth, the raising of his station, and honoring him; where the first and the last gathered, and all the prophets, messengers, all the angels, and those brought near, and the calamity became widespread and the terror intensified, and everyone was preoccupied with himself, fearful, awestruck at the majesty of the great Lord, kneeling on his knees; because of what he sees on that day of tremendous danger and terror, and no one dares on that terrible day to address the Lord, Blessed and Most High, to remove anything that has descended... except His servant and the Seal of His Messengers, the bride of His kingdom, its secret and its elixir, the master of all that our Lord, Majestic and Exalted, created – peace and blessings be upon him – and he says when the people come to him seeking intercession to the Lord, Blessed and Most High: 'I am for it' – he does not fear, nor does the matter of his self concern him, nor does he stammer, and he goes until he prostrates beneath the Throne, and then the Lord, Majestic and Exalted, says: 'Raise your head, O Muhammad, and speak, you will be heard; ask, you will be given; intercede, you will be granted intercession.' So consider, may God have mercy on you, this dear, gentle, noble address to him (peace and blessings be upon him) from our Lord, Blessed and Most High, on that terrible day, on which He, glorified be He, became angry with an anger the like of which He has never been angry before, nor will He be angry with its like afterwards – how is it not clear in meaning, without dispute, doubt, or possibility, that there is none more honored than our Prophet, our master, our lord Muhammad (peace and blessings be upon him) with God, Blessed and Most High?! And in the hadith: 'He (peace and blessings be upon him) is the first to knock at the gate of Paradise, and Ridwan, its keeper (peace be upon him), says: Who? He says: Muhammad.'
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a combined argument and narrative affirming the Prophet Muhammad's absolute superiority over all creation. The author begins by noting the unification of nations under Islam, then states that the previous scriptures' testimonies to the Prophet's prophethood and honor are countless and clearer than the sun. He then declares that consensus (ijma') has been established on the Prophet's superiority, with evidence from the Qur'an and Sunnah being abundant. To illustrate this, he presents the universally acknowledged event of the Great Intercession (al-shafa'a al-kubra) on the Day of Judgment. In that dreadful assembly of all creatures, only the Prophet dares to approach God for intercession, and he does so with confidence. God addresses him with honor and grants him intercession. The author calls the reader to reflect on this divine address as proof that no one is more honored by God than Muhammad. He adds a hadith that the Prophet will be the first to knock on the gate of Paradise. The overall argument is that consensus and the specific narrative of intercession leave no room for doubt about the Prophet's supreme rank.

الشفاعة الكبرى

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Prophet's superiority is merely a matter of personal devotion, but the author grounds it in consensus and explicit divine action.
Correction: The intercession narrative shows God directly honoring the Prophet, and consensus confirms this universally.

The Prophet's Authority Over the Fire
Sanusi describes the Fire's approach, the necks, and the Prophet's intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's intercession on the Day of Judgment demonstrates his unique authority over the Fire, as depicted in the Salaf's narrative.

Core Idea
The Prophet commands the Fire, and it obeys.

This lesson presents a vivid description of the Fire's terror on the Day of Judgment and the Prophet's decisive role in restraining it. The narrative, while not a matter of creed per se, illustrates the honor granted to the Prophet by Allah, showing that even the Fire submits to his command.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative of the Fire
Read the Arabic passage describing the Fire being driven, its approach, and the emergence of necks. Notice the dramatic details.
The lengths mentioned (500 years) are symbolic of immense scale.
2
Identify the Prophet's action
Find where the Prophet rises, rebukes the Fire, and commands it to retreat. Observe the divine response: the Fire hears a command to listen to him.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider what this narrative teaches about the Prophet's rank. How does it relate to his intercession?
This authority is a sign of his honor and closeness to Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَيَقُولُ رِضْوَانُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ : بِكَ أُمِرْتُ أَلا أَفْتَحَ لِأَحَدٍ قَبْلَكَ » أو كما قال . ورُوِيَ ما معناه : أنَّ النارَ عندَ ما تسوقها الملائكة الموكَّلون بها بالسلاسل لتحيط بالخلْقِ في المحشرِ ، فاذا قَرُبَتْ منهم بنحو خمس مئة سنةٍ تَشْهَقُ شهيقاً عظيماً منكراً، وتتفلَّتُ منها الأعناق إلى المحشرِ ، طولُ العُنُقِ خمس مئة سنة ، لهُ فم وأسنانٌ مِنْ نارٍ ، فيصل العنق إلى المحشرِ ويَزْفِرُ عليهم ويَشْهَقُ عليهم شهيقاً منكراً لا يستطاع سماعُه ، ويملأُ عليهم الجوَّ ظلمةً وناراً زيادةً على ما هم فيهِ مِنَ الأهوالِ الجسيمةِ ، ويلتقط العنقُ الناسَ مِنَ الموقفِ ويبتلعُهُم في ذلكَ العنق الطويل إلى جوفه ! وحينئذ تجثو على الرُّكَب الملائكة المقرَّبون والأنبياء والرُّسُلُ على جميعهم م الصلاة والسلام ، فحينئذ ينهضُ إلى النارِ نبينا وسيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، فيزجرُها عنِ الناسِ ، ويأمرُها بالتأخُرِ عنهم ، فتسمعُ النارُ حينئذ نداءً مِنْ قِبَلِ اللهِ تبارك وتعالى : اسمعي له وأطيعي . وقد رُوِيَ عنهُ أَنَّهُ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ قالَ : « أَنَا سَيْدُ وَلَدِ آدَمَ ، وأَنَا سَيْدُ النَّاسِ ، وآدَمُ فَمَنْ دُونَهُ تَحْتَ لِوَانِي يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ ، و« لَوْ كَانَ مُوسَى وَعِيسَى حَيَّيْنِ مَا وَسِعَهُمَا إِلا اتباعي وبالجملة : فثبوت شرفِهِ وأفضليَّتِهِ على جميع المخلوقاتِ يكادُ أنْ يكون معلوماً مِنَ الدين ضرورةً ؛ بحيثُ لا يُحتاجُ إلى سردِ دليل . وَلَيْسَ يَصِحُ فِي الْأَذْهَانِ شَيْءٌ مَتَى أَحْتَاجَ النَّهَارُ إِلَى دَلِيلِ
Ridwan, peace be upon him, says: 'I was commanded not to open for anyone before you' – or as he said. And it is related in meaning: that when the Fire is driven by the angels entrusted with it with chains to surround the creation in the gathering-place, and when it approaches them to about five hundred years, it gives a great, terrible gasp, and necks burst forth from it to the gathering-place, the length of the neck being five hundred years, having a mouth and teeth of fire. Then the neck reaches the gathering-place and blows upon them and gasps upon them a terrible gasp that cannot be heard, and fills the air upon them with darkness and fire in addition to the tremendous terrors they are in. And the neck snatches people from the standing-place and swallows them into its interior through that long neck. Then the near-stationed angels, the prophets, and the messengers – upon all of them be prayer and peace – fall on their knees. Then our Prophet, our Master, our Patron Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, rises up to the Fire, rebukes it for the people, and commands it to retreat from them. Then the Fire hears a call from Allah, Blessed and Exalted: 'Listen to him and obey.' And it has been related from him that he, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'I am the master of the children of Adam, and I am the master of mankind, and Adam and whoever is beneath him are under my banner on the Day of Resurrection.' And he said: 'If Moses and Jesus were alive, they would have no choice but to follow me.' In summary: the proof of his honor and his superiority over all creatures is almost known from religion by necessity, such that there is no need to adduce evidence. And nothing is correct in minds that needs the day for proof.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is a combined narrative and doctrinal statement. It begins by reporting a saying of Ridwan, the guardian of Paradise, who states that he was commanded not to open Paradise for anyone before the Prophet – this indicates the Prophet's precedence even over the entry to Paradise. Then it relates a description of the Fire on the Day of Judgment. The angels drive the Fire with chains; when it comes within five hundred years' distance, it gives a terrible gasp. Necks emerge from the Fire, each five hundred years long, with mouths and teeth of fire. These necks reach the gathering place, blow and gasp terrifyingly, fill the air with darkness and fire, and snatch people, swallowing them. At that point, the angels, prophets, and messengers fall to their knees. Then the Prophet Muhammad (saw) rises, rebukes the Fire, and commands it to retreat. The Fire hears a divine command to listen to him and obey. This demonstrates the Prophet's authority over even the Fire. The passage then cites two hadith: one where he declares himself master of all descendants of Adam and master of mankind, with Adam and others under his banner; another where he says that if Moses and Jesus were alive, they would have to follow him – indicating his supremacy over all prophets. The author concludes that the Prophet's honor and superiority over all creatures is so evident that it is known from religion by necessity, requiring no proof. He quotes a line of poetry: 'Nothing is correct in minds that needs the day for proof,' meaning that self-evident truths need no demonstration.

Proof of the Prophet's Superiority Over All Creation
Sanusi cites hadiths and a concluding statement proving the Prophet's superiority by necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet Muhammad's superiority over all creation is established through explicit prophetic hadiths and is considered a necessary knowledge from the religion.

Core Idea
The Prophet's superiority is a self-evident truth of Islam.

Sanusi presents compelling evidence for the Prophet's unmatched status. He cites multiple authentic hadiths where the Prophet himself declares his mastery, and then argues that this truth is so evident within Islam that it requires no elaborate proof. This lesson explores those hadiths and the powerful conclusion that follows.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadiths carefully
List the four hadiths that the author quotes. Notice how each one asserts the Prophet's supremacy over different categories: children of Adam, mankind, Adam and others under his banner, and even Moses and Jesus would have to follow him.
These hadiths are the core textual evidence.
2
Understand the concluding statement
Pay attention to the author's conclusion: the Prophet's superiority is 'almost known from religion by necessity.' Reflect on what that means — that it is so clear it doesn't need detailed proof.
This is a key concept in kalam: knowledge by necessity.
3
Analyze the poetic line
Read the final line from al-Mutanabbi. It says that nothing is accepted in minds when daylight itself needs a proof. How does this analogy reinforce the author's argument?
The poet is comparing the Prophet's status to daylight — self-evident.
4
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to ensure you grasp the main point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد رُوِيَ عنهُ أَنَّهُ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ قالَ : « أَنَا سَيْدُ وَلَدِ آدَمَ (۱) ، وا أَنَا سَيْدُ النَّاسِ (۲) ، وا آدَمُ فَمَنْ دُونَهُ تَحْتَ لِوَانِي يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ (٣) ، و« لَوْ كَانَ مُوسَى وَعِيسَى حَيَّيْنِ مَا وَسِعَهُمَا إِلا اتباعي (٤) || وبالجملة : فثبوت شرفِهِ وأفضليَّتِهِ على جميع المخلوقاتِ يكادُ أنْ يكون معلوماً مِنَ الدين ضرورةً ؛ بحيثُ لا يُحتاجُ إلى سردِ دليل . وَلَيْسَ يَصِحُ فِي الْأَذْهَانِ شَيْءٌ مَتَى أَحْتَاجَ النَّهَارُ إِلَى دَلِيلِ(٥)
And it has been narrated from him that he ﷺ said: 'I am the master of the children of Adam (1), and I am the master of mankind (2), and Adam and whoever is beneath him will be under my banner on the Day of Resurrection (3), and 'If Moses and Jesus were alive, they would have no recourse but to follow me (4).' And in summary: the establishment of his honor and superiority over all creatures is almost known from religion by necessity; such that there is no need to list a proof. And nothing is correct in minds when the day needs a proof (5).

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the Prophet Muhammad's superiority over all creation. It begins by citing four hadiths that directly assert his preeminence: he is the master of Adam's children, the master of mankind, and on the Day of Resurrection Adam and all others will be under his banner; moreover, if Moses and Jesus were alive, they would have no choice but to follow him. After these narrations, the author concludes that the Prophet's honor and superiority (sharaf and afdaliyya) are nearly known from the religion by necessity (ḍarūra), so that one does not need to produce a detailed proof. The passage ends with a poetic line from al-Mutanabbi, reinforcing the idea that just as daylight is self-evident and needs no proof, the Prophet's superiority is similarly evident. The author thus presents a concise argument: the Prophet's status is so manifest that it is a necessary knowledge derived directly from the religion.

Opinions on the Best Prophet After Muhammad
Sanusi quotes al-Taftazani listing five opinions on the best prophet after Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the differing scholarly opinions on who is the best prophet after Muhammad and the reasons given for each.

Core Idea
Even after consensus on Muhammad's supremacy, scholars disagreed on the next best prophet.

This lesson presents a fascinating glimpse into classical Islamic theological debate. While there is unanimous agreement that Prophet Muhammad ﷺ is the best of all prophets and messengers, scholars held various views on who holds that rank after him. Al-Taftazani records five distinct opinions, each supported by a specific virtue or characteristic of the prophet in question. As you read the passage, notice both the diversity of opinion and the types of arguments used.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English carefully. Observe the structure: consensus statement, then five opinions introduced by 'قيل' (it was said).
Pay attention to the phrasing used for each opinion.
2
Identify each opinion and its reasoning
List the five prophets and the reason given for each. Consider why these specific virtues were highlighted.
3
Reflect on the significance
Think about why this disagreement matters for Islamic theology. Does it affect other beliefs?
The passage does not resolve the debate, only reports it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیهان الأول في بيان الفاضل بعده عليه الصلاة والسلام ] قال التفتازاني في ( شرح المقاصدِ الدينية » لهُ بعدما ذكرَ الإجماع على أنَّهُ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أفضل الأنبياء والرُّسُل عليهم الصلاة والسلام : ( اختلفوا في الأفضل بعده : فقيل : آدم عليه السلام ؛ لكونه أبا البشر وقيل : نوح عليه السلام ؛ لطول عبادتِهِ ومجاهدته . وقيل : إبراهيم عليه السلام ؛ لزيادة توكَّلِهِ واصطفائِهِ وقيل : موسى عليهِ السلامُ ؛ لكونه كليم الله تعالى ونجيَّهُ • وقيل : عيسى عليهِ السلامُ ؛ لكونِهِ رُوحَ اللَّهِ تعالى وصفيَّهُ )(۱)
Two Notices: The First: On explaining the one who is best after him ﷺ. Al-Taftazani said in his 'Sharh al-Maqasid al-Diniyya' after mentioning the consensus that he ﷺ is the best of the prophets and messengers, peace be upon them: 'They differed on the best after him. So it was said: Adam, peace be upon him, because he is the father of mankind. And it was said: Noah, peace be upon him, because of the length of his worship and striving. And it was said: Abraham, peace be upon him, because of his increased trust and chosenness. And it was said: Moses, peace be upon him, because he is the speaker of Allah and His intimate. And it was said: Jesus, peace be upon him, because he is the spirit of Allah and His chosen one.'
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is the first of two 'notices' (tanbīh). It reports a citation from al-Taftazani's Sharh al-Maqasid al-Diniyya. After noting that there is consensus on the Prophet Muhammad being the best of all prophets and messengers, Taftazani records that scholars differed on who is the best (al-afḍal) after him. The passage enumerates five distinct opinions, each with a brief reason: (1) Adam, because he is the father of mankind; (2) Noah, because of his long worship and striving; (3) Abraham, because of his increased trust and being chosen; (4) Moses, because he is the speaker of Allah (kalīm Allāh) and His intimate; (5) Jesus, because he is the spirit of Allah (rūḥ Allāh) and His chosen one. The author does not endorse any of these views; he simply presents the disagreement.

الأفضل بعده (al-afḍal ba'dahu)
آدم
نوح
إبراهيم
موسى
عيسى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: There is consensus on who is the best prophet after Muhammad.
Correction: In fact, scholars differed; five opinions are recorded in this passage.

Superiority Among Prophets is by God's Decree Without Cause
Sanusi defines the nature of superiority among prophets and angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi insists that superiority among prophets is solely by God's decree and not due to any inherent cause in the prophets themselves.

Core Idea
Superiority among prophets is by God's sovereign will alone, not by merit.

Sanusi tackles a sensitive theological question: why are some prophets superior to others? He warns against attributing superiority to personal virtues, which would imply that God's choice is constrained. Instead, he grounds superiority purely in God's decree, using an analogy of a master and his slaves to illustrate divine sovereignty. As you read, notice how he carefully distinguishes God's transcendence from human limitations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Pay attention to the key terms: الأفضلية, العِلَّة المُوجِبَة.
The Arabic is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the main claim
Identify Sanusi's main claim: superiority is by God's decree, not by a necessitating cause.
3
Analyze the analogy
Examine the analogy of a master preferring one slave over another. What does this illustrate? How does Sanusi qualify it?
The analogy is approximate because human masters have motives.
4
Understand the rejection
Understand why Sanusi rejects the view that superiority is due to different attributes. Note his warning about poor manners.

Source Text

الأفضلية التي ثبتَتْ بينَ الأنبياء والرُّسُلِ ، وفي معناهم الملائكة ، على جميعهم الصلاة والسلام ، قال : ( إِنَّما وقعَتِ الأفضلية بينهم بحكم الله تعالى بأفضليّةِ بعضهم على بعض ، لا مِنْ أجلِ عِلَّةٍ مُوجِبةٍ لذلكَ وُجِدَتْ في الفاضلِ وفُقِدَتْ مِنَ المفضولِ ، وللسيّدِ أَنْ يُفضّلَ بعض عبيده على بعض وإنْ كانَ كلُّ واحدٍ منهم كاملاً في نفسِهِ ، بالغاً مِنْ ذلكَ الغاية التي تليقُ بهِ ، مِنْ غيرِ أنْ يحمله على ذلك وصف يكون فيهم وذلكَ ممَّا يجب له بحقِّ سيادتِهِ ، والتمثيل بالسيد أمر تقريبي ؛ إذ لا يخلو مِنَ البواعثِ والأغراض ، والله تعالى مُنزَّه عن جميع ذلك . ثمَّ إِنَّ الله تعالى أعلم بما يقتضيه هذا الحكم بالأفضلية ، فهذا هو الذي يظهر لي في سبب وجود الأفضلية بين الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام ، ولا يتصوَّرُ عندي إنكار لذلك . وأمَّا أَنْ يُعتقَدَ في سبب وجود الأفضلية اتصافُ الفاضل بصفاتٍ هي مفقودة في المفضولِ ، أو أنَّ صفاتِ الفاضل ناقصةٌ وصفاتِ الأفضل كاملة .. فهو عندي تكلف وتعشف ، ولا يَسلَمُ مِنَ الوقوع في سوء الأدب .
The superiority that is established among the prophets and messengers, and in their meaning the angels, upon all of them blessings and peace, he said: 'Indeed, the superiority among them occurred by the decree of God Most High, by His preferring some of them over others, not because of a necessitating cause found in the superior and lacking in the inferior. And it is permissible for a master to prefer some of his slaves over others even if each of them is perfect in himself, having reached the utmost degree befitting him, without being impelled to that by a description that exists in them. And that is something obligatory for him by right of his mastery. And the analogy with the master is an approximation, for it is not free of motives and purposes, and God Most High is transcendent above all that.' Then indeed God Most High knows best what this judgment of superiority necessitates. This is what appears to me regarding the reason for the existence of superiority among the prophets, upon them blessings and peace, and I cannot conceive of denying that. As for the belief that the reason for the existence of superiority is the superior's being qualified by attributes that are lacking in the inferior, or that the attributes of the superior are deficient and the attributes of the more excellent are perfect... that is, in my view, affectation and strain, and it does not escape falling into poor manners.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the nature of superiority among prophets and angels. It begins by stating that superiority is by God's decree alone, not due to any necessitating cause (عِلَّة مُوجِبَة) inherent in the superior person. Sanusi then offers an analogy: a master may prefer one slave over another even if both are equally perfect, without any external reason—simply by right of his mastery. However, Sanusi notes that this analogy is approximate (تقريبي) because human masters have motives, whereas God is transcendent (مُنزَّه) above all such. He then concludes that the true reason for superiority is known only to God. Finally, he rejects the alternative view that superiority stems from the superior possessing additional or better attributes, calling such a view an affectation (تكلف) that leads to disrespect.

Key Terms
الأفضلية
العِلَّة المُوجِبَة
التقريب
المُنزَّه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Superiority among prophets is due to their greater virtues or closer relationship with God.
Correction: Sanusi argues that superiority is purely by God's decree and not caused by any attribute in the superior person.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why does one prophet have superiority over another?
A) Because the superior prophet has more virtues.
B) Because God decrees it without a necessitating cause.
C) Because the superior prophet works harder.
D) Because the inferior prophet lacks certain attributes.

Key Takeaway
Superiority among prophets is a matter of God's sovereign decree, not human merit or attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at the differences in people's abilities, status, or faith, do you secretly believe that these reflect something they 'deserve' based on their own efforts or qualities? How does this lesson challenge that assumption, and what would it mean for you to truly submit to God's absolute sovereignty without needing to understand the reason?
?
Are you willing to accept that God may prefer some of His servants over others—even those you consider less pious or less knowledgeable—without any cause you can perceive? What does your reaction to this reveal about your heart's attachment to your own understanding of justice?
?
Sanusi warns that attributing superiority to personal attributes leads to 'poor manners' towards God. Examine your own conversations about the Prophets or righteous people: do you ever unconsciously reduce their rank to their deeds or character? How can you revere them without imposing human frameworks on God's choices?
